- AC #6 process-kill recovery ✅ verified: BEFORE PID 1734382 -> sudo kill -9 -> AFTER PID 1737523 (different = restart confirmed); state active; uptime advanced to 08:11:37 CDT; /api/v1/health 200; recovery time ~10s (5s RestartSec + uvicorn warmup). Bundled bash test 5/5 PASS post-recovery.
- AC #7 host-reboot survival: deferred to CIO discretion ('if CIO willing' per story spec). Procedure documented in docs/testing.md.

### Operator deploy regression (caught + fixed mid-deploy):
- First `bash deploy/deploy-server.sh` run failed silently: `sudo: a terminal is required to read the password` because the SSH heredoc for step 4.7 install lacked TTY allocation. The remote shell had no `set -e`, so the misleading 'Unit installed + daemon-reload + enabled.' echo printed even though all 3 sudo commands had failed. Step 5 cutover pkill (using my new `nohup .*[u]vicorn` pattern) only matched the bash wrapper, leaving the detached uvicorn child alive on PID 1073743. Step 6 sudo systemctl restart also failed silently. Net: server state unchanged; legacy nohup still serving.
- Fixed in same session via 3 changes to deploy-server.sh: (a) `ssh -t $HOST` for sudo-bearing commands so sudo can prompt the operator interactively; (b) `set -e` inside the install heredoc so sudo failures actually halt instead of falling through to misleading success-echo; (c) smarter step 5 cutover gated on `systemctl is-active --quiet` so subsequent deploys skip the orphan kill (preventing race with own systemctl restart) AND uses the broader `[u]vicorn src.server.main:app` pkill pattern that catches both the bash nohup wrapper AND the detached uvicorn child (the prior `nohup .*[u]vicorn` only matched the wrapper, leaving the child alive).
- Operator re-ran deploy-server.sh with the patched script. Sudo prompted 4x (3 in install + 1 in restart) and worked end-to-end. Health check passed; obd-server.service active; cutover complete.

### Files changed (this session, post-flip):
- Modified: deploy/deploy-server.sh (ssh -t + set -e + smarter cutover; ~3 hunks)
- Modified: offices/ralph/sprint.json (US-231 passes:true + completedDate + completionNotes addendum)
- Modified: offices/ralph/progress.txt (this entry)
- Modified: offices/ralph/ralph_agents.json (Rex unassigned + Session 105 cont. close)

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **`ssh -t` is required for ANY sudo-bearing remote command.** Without -t, ssh runs the remote shell without a controlling TTY, and sudo cannot prompt for a password. The error is loud (`a terminal is required`), but if the remote shell has no `set -e`, subsequent commands run anyway -- including misleading success-echos. Both invariants belong in the deploy template: -t for the ssh AND set -e inside the heredoc. Not one or the other.
- **pkill patterns must account for detached children.** `nohup cmd &` creates a bash wrapper that holds the literal `nohup ...` cmdline + a detached child that ONLY has the original cmd's cmdline. Killing the wrapper does NOT kill the child (that's the whole point of nohup). When you write a pkill cmdline pattern, decide which process you actually want dead and pattern-match against ITS cmdline. The broader `[u]vicorn src.server.main:app` pattern matches both processes; the narrower `nohup .*[u]vicorn` only matches the wrapper. For cutover correctness, broader > narrower.
- **Conditional cutover beats one-time-only cutover.** First plan was 'pkill the orphan once on first deploy; subsequent deploys skip because the pattern won't match systemd-managed cmdline.' Reality: the pattern DID match systemd-managed cmdline (uvicorn cmdline is the same regardless of who launched it). Better pattern: gate the pkill on `systemctl is-active --quiet obd-server.service` -- explicit 'cutover only when not yet systemd-managed' -- which is robust against future ambiguity.
- **Live-test the kill drill in the same session as the deploy.** AC #6 (process-kill recovery) is the actual proof Restart=always works. Without running it, you have a `Restart=always` directive + a hope. Running the drill takes 30 seconds (capture PID + sudo kill + sleep 10 + verify new PID) and catches any unit-config typo or systemd flap-protection misconfiguration immediately. Worth the 30 seconds every time, not just on the first deploy.
- **The Bash tool can't allocate a TTY.** When testing patches that use `ssh -t`, the local Bash tool execution will fail with 'Pseudo-terminal will not be allocated because stdin is not a terminal.' This is fine -- the operator running the same command from their interactive shell DOES have a TTY and will get the sudo prompt as designed. The lesson: don't try to validate `ssh -t` flow from the agent side; document the operator-side workflow and trust the patch.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pre-flight scout the sudo gate.** A 1-second `sudo -n true` SSH call answers "can this windows-dev session do live install + restart" definitively. Knowing the answer up front lets you scope the story correctly (build code-side, document the operator-needed steps in docs/testing.md, mark AC partial-pass) rather than discovering the gate at the last minute. Add this probe to any deploy-touching story's pre-flight checklist.
- **Skip semantics for deploy-pending state, not just SSH-unreachable.** US-230's pattern only skips on SSH unreachable; if the deploy step hadn't run yet, the test would FAIL (because the journald change wouldn't be applied). For US-231 I extended the skip gate: "SSH reachable BUT unit not installed" -> exit 77 with a clear "deploy not yet run" message + reference to deploy-server.sh. This pattern keeps fast suite green during the in-flight-deploy window without hiding the gap (skip reason mentions US-231 + the operator command).
- **Cutover pattern: kill the orphan, then start systemd, never both running.** The pkill BEFORE systemctl start is the one-time-needed safety net to clear the pre-systemd nohup process. Subsequent deploys are no-op for the pkill (nohup-wrapped pattern doesn't match the systemd-managed cmdline) but the line stays in deploy-server.sh because (a) cheap, (b) defensive against operator manual-restart accidents.
- **Modern systemd flap protection MUST live in [Unit].** StartLimitIntervalSec + StartLimitBurst in [Service] generates a deprecation warning and is silently ignored on newer systemd. Both the Pi-side eclipse-obd.service (US-210) and now obd-server.service follow the [Unit]-block pattern. test_obdServerService_flapProtectionInUnitSection asserts this so a future edit can't regress.
- **Stale parallel files are common archeology.** Found 2 pre-US-231 deploy files (different name, wrong paths, wrong policy) that pre-dated the actual server config. Per CIO Q1 rule, filed TD-037 rather than auto-deleting. The TD lays out the cleanup as a Sprint 19 candidate. Watch for this pattern: any 'deploy/foo.service' file from project-init time likely has wrong defaults; verify against the live server before assuming it works.
- **systemctl restart fails the deploy when the service can't come up.** The 2s sleep + is-active check in step 6 is the right place to fail loud (operator sees it immediately) rather than later when the health-check fails (ambiguous: was it a startup error or a downstream issue?). The is-active probe + journalctl pointer gives the operator the right next command for triage.
- **Always anchor static-text tests on semantic markers, not implementation literals.** Pre-existing `test_migrationStep_runsBeforeServiceStart` searched for `uvicorn src.server.main:app --host` -- a literal that became invalid the moment I moved the start logic into the systemd unit. Fix was one-line: anchor on `systemctl restart obd-server` instead, which is the new semantic marker for "service start." Lesson: when writing static-text tests against deploy scripts, prefer markers that survive refactors (function names, comment markers, `# Step N:` headers) over literal command lines.
- **B-044 hardcoded-address audit fires on hostname strings, not just IPs.** The `chi-srv-01` literal in my new install step (a warning-message string) tripped the audit. Fix: use `${SERVER_HOSTNAME}` from addresses.sh (the canonical source). The audit's broader signal: any new operational text that names an env-specific identifier should resolve through addresses.sh rather than hardcoding -- even in `echo` warning output, because rename costs are real.
- **Self-inflicted-regression-during-deploy-script-edit is the high-frequency pattern.** Both regressions came from changing the deploy script. The deploy script is heavily test-anchored (migration gate + B-044 audit + future tests), so editing it without running the full fast suite first is asking for a follow-up cycle. Should default to running the full fast suite as the LAST step before claiming verification, not piecewise targeted runs -- the fast suite catches what targeted runs miss.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Truncate scripts are operational snapshots, not reusable libraries.** Each truncate (US-205, US-227) captures the policy at a specific moment in time -- the WHERE clause, drive_counter target, sync gate threshold, sentinel name, pollution window are all moment-specific. The reusable surface is the SUBPROCESS PLUMBING (SSH, backups, fixture hash, service control). Importing the helpers via `importlib.util.spec_from_file_location` from a sibling script gives you the plumbing without making the policy modules siblings; the new script reads top-to-bottom as a clean operational record. This pattern should be the template for the inevitable US-NNN truncate in Sprint 21+.
- **Sync gate as a divergenceDetected reason.** Treating "sync_log cursor regressed" the same as "fixture hash mismatch" gives the script a uniform refuse-and-explain failure mode. Future ops scripts should follow the divergenceDetected pattern -- a list of reasons that, if non-empty, blocks --execute with the operator-facing reason printed verbatim. Beats single-purpose if/else gates.
- **Data-driven table enumeration over hardcoded lists.** US-205 hardcoded its 4 tables; US-227 enumerated tables with both (drive_id, data_source) columns. The enumerate-and-no-op approach gracefully handles future drift: if a new capture table gets added with both columns, the next truncate picks it up without needing to be told. The cost is one extra SQL probe per table (cheap). Worth the future-proofing for any operational script that targets "rows matching a property."
- **Idempotent counter advance via WHERE-guarded UPDATE.** `UPDATE drive_counter SET last_drive_id=3 WHERE id=1 AND last_drive_id<3` is the single SQL idiom that makes "advance to N, never regress" trivial. Re-runs are no-ops without needing a SELECT-then-decide round trip. This idiom belongs in any future "advance counter to high-water" script (Spool's analytics state, sync cursors, etc.).
- **The sync_log cursor is the cheapest deploy-state oracle.** Confirmed AGAIN this session (Session 104 BLOCKED diagnosis, Session 105 close diagnosis): one SSH `sqlite3 ... 'SELECT * FROM sync_log'` tells you when the Pi last pushed, what tables are stuck, and whether new drives have piled up. This is faster than tailing journalctl, more reliable than greping deploy markers, and works even when the Pi service is in a BT-retry loop. Add it to any sprint-status script you ever write.
- **Backup-before-DELETE belongs in the script, not a runbook.** The `backupPi` + `backupServer` calls run automatically before any DELETE; if either fails, SafetyGateError aborts before any row is touched. This is the right place for that safety net -- relying on operator memory ("did I backup?") is how you lose Drive 3 someday. The 509 MB SQLite snapshot + 1.9 MB mysqldump together cost <30 seconds; cheap insurance.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pi sync_log is the authoritative deploy-state oracle.** Any sprint story whose acceptance is "X has reached the server" can be pre-flight-checked in one SSH call: `sqlite3 ~/Projects/Eclipse-01/data/obd.db 'SELECT * FROM sync_log; SELECT drive_id, data_source, COUNT(*) FROM realtime_data GROUP BY drive_id, data_source'`. The cursor freeze date + per-drive_id row counts together tell you (a) when the Pi last pushed, (b) whether new drives have piled up since, and (c) whether US-226-style auto-sync is alive. Faster than reading journalctl, more reliable than greping deploy markers.
- **Deploy gates aren't hardware gates -- but they walk + quack like one.** The Sprint 13 BL-006 precedent (CIO + car required) and this BL-007 (CIO + deploy required) share the same shape: code-only paths exhausted, real-world action required, no partial credit available. Treating "deploy hasn't happened" as a hard blocker -- exactly like "engine isn't running" -- preserves story integrity vs. silent-pre-build temptation.
- **Source-tree markers are the cheapest deploy-state probe.** `grep -c '_maybeTriggerIntervalSync\|_initializeSyncClient' src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/{core,lifecycle}.py` over SSH against the deployed checkout: 0 = not deployed, >0 = deployed. Cheaper than re-running validate_config or smoke-testing the service. Pick a unique-enough symbol from the diff and grep for it; works for any "did the new code make it" question.
- **Refusal-rule discipline pays compounding interest across sessions.** Session 103 flagged exactly this blocker in its closeout note; Session 104 confirmed it 4 days later. Without that handoff signal, this session would have either (a) wasted cycles re-discovering the gate or (b) speculatively pre-built the script and risked Drive 3. The ralph_agents.json `note` field doing its handoff job.

## 2026-04-23 - US-233 - pre-mint orphan-row backfill for Drive 3 (Session 103, Rex / Agent 1)
Task: Close Spool's Sprint 17 consolidated Section 9 (P2). Drive 3 has 225 NULL-drive_id rows tagged data_source='real' from the 39-second BT-connect-to-cranking window (16:36:10..49Z) that landed before EngineStateMachine minted drive_id=3 at 16:36:50Z. Three policy options offered: (a) post-hoc backfill script, (b) provisional drive_id at BT-connect with reconciliation at CRANKING, (c) document NULL as authoritative policy. Picked (a) for: lowest risk vs stopConditions[2,3] (no live state-machine change -> can't break US-219 review ritual or US-214 dual-writer); reuses Sprint 15 truncate_session23.py safety patterns; concrete value for Spool (re-tagged rows become part of Drive 3's per-drive analytics).

### Pre-flight audit (AC #1):
- SSH probe to chi-eclipse-01 sqlite3 returned 413 NULL-drive_id real rows total: 225 in 2026-04-23T16:36:10..49Z (Spool's count exact; 221 of 225 fall in the precise 39-sec window, other 4 at edges); 188 separate rows on 2026-04-21 (pre-US-212 pollution era, no subsequent drive within any cap; out of US-233 scope).
- Confirmed drive_id distribution: drive_id=1 has 2,939,090 real rows (US-227 target); drive_id=3 has 6,089 real rows (legitimate Drive 3 from 16:36:50..18:35:44Z).
- Identified follow-up: 188 pollution rows won't be caught by US-227's drive_id=1 filter (they are NULL drive_id); flagged in Spool inbox closure note for post-US-227 cleanup.

### What was implemented:
- **scripts/backfill_premint_orphans.py** (NEW, ~380 LOC): pure-function core (scanOrphans, scanDriveStarts, findOrphanBackfillMatches, applyBackfill, renderReport) + CLI (main) + safety helpers (backupDatabase, sentinel read/write/clear). Frozen-slots dataclasses OrphanRow / DriveStart / BackfillMatch. Exception hierarchy BackfillError -> SafetyCapError. Algorithm: orphan -> nearest subsequent real drive_id whose MIN(timestamp) is within --window-seconds (default 60s); orphans with no subsequent drive within cap stay NULL. CLI: --db PATH required, --dry-run / --execute mutex required, --window-seconds N (default 60), --max-orphans-per-drive N (default 1000), --sentinel-dir DIR (defaults to db parent). --execute refuses without prior --dry-run sentinel; backupDatabase copies obd.db -> obd.db.bak-us233-<ts> before any UPDATE; UPDATE wrapped in BEGIN IMMEDIATE / COMMIT with try-rollback. UPDATE WHERE clause requires drive_id IS NULL AND data_source='real' so a stale BackfillMatch can't clobber a tagged row even if passed in. Scope strictly realtime_data only -- drive_summary / connection_log / statistics / alert_log untouched.
- **tests/pi/obdii/test_premint_orphan_backfill.py** (NEW, 30 tests across 6 classes): synthesizes SQLite in-memory; no SSH, no real Pi. TestScanOrphans (4) -- empty DB, NULL+real-only filter, sim/test exclusion, timestamp sort. TestScanDriveStarts (3) -- empty DB, MIN(timestamp) per drive_id, sim-only drives excluded. TestFindOrphanBackfillMatches (10) -- empty DB, in-window match, out-of-window reject, at-or-after-drive-start reject, between-two-drives -> nearest-subsequent, real Drive 3 225-row scenario, 188 pollution scenario, custom 30s window boundaries, ValueError on windowSeconds<=0. TestApplyBackfill (6) -- empty matches=0 noop, UPDATE applies + return count, idempotent second-run=0, WHERE-guard refuses tagged-row clobber, sim orphans untouched, drive_summary unmodified. TestApplyBackfillSafety (1) -- per-drive cap raises SafetyCapError. TestCli (6) -- dry-run no-op, execute-without-sentinel refuses, execute-after-dry-run applies, mutex enforcement, no-mode-flag exits, execute on already-clean DB succeeds.
- **specs/architecture.md Section 5**: new 'Pre-mint orphan policy (US-233)' subsection inserted between US-229 drive-end detection and Migration. Documents the option (a) decision with explicit rejection rationale for (b) and (c), then enumerates 6 backfill invariants (idempotent / hard cap window / per-drive safety cap / tagged rows inviolate / scope realtime_data only / Session 23 fixture out-of-scope).
- **docs/testing.md**: new 'Backfilling pre-mint orphan rows (CIO-facing, US-233)' section before Modification History. 6-step CIO procedure (SSH -> stop service -> dry-run -> inspect report -> execute -> restart service); safety gates summary; off-Pi test coverage pointer; 'what the script does NOT do' scope-limit list (no server propagation, no other capture tables, no live engine_state change). Modification History entry added at top.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern: when a story offers multiple policy options, lean on stopConditions to disambiguate.** US-233 listed (a/b/c). stopConditions[2,3] explicitly named (b)'s downstream risks (US-200 transitions affecting US-219 review ritual + US-214 dual-writer). Reading stopConditions BEFORE picking the option made the choice obvious -- don't go straight to the option that sounds cleanest, read the bail-out list first.
- **Pattern: 'listen to the test' moment caught a real test fixture issue, not a code bug.** Original test_doesNotTouchTaggedRows asserted both 'tagged rows stay tagged' AND 'orphan goes to drive 3' in the same scenario, but had drive_id=99 row INSIDE the candidate window. Matcher correctly picked drive_id=99 (nearest subsequent) instead of drive_id=3, surfacing the conflated test. Fix: split into two focused tests -- one for the WHERE-guard safety invariant (passing a stale BackfillMatch directly + asserting UPDATE refuses), one for nearest-subsequent matching (already covered by test_orphansBetweenTwoDrives_attachToNearestSubsequent). Lesson: when one test asserts two unrelated properties, splitting it usually reveals which is the real check.
- **Pattern: synthesize the actual real-world scenario as a test.** test_drive3Scenario_225rowsIn39SecWindowAllMatched mirrors the exact production data shape -- 225 rows over 39 seconds, drive 3 starts 1s after the last orphan, expect all 225 match. This catches semantics issues that a smaller synthesized scenario would miss (e.g., off-by-one on the boundary timestamp). Also captures the production count as a regression invariant -- if the algorithm or boundary semantics ever drift, the test fails with a clear narrative.
- **Pattern: pure-function core + thin CLI wrapper for testability.** scanOrphans / findOrphanBackfillMatches / applyBackfill take a sqlite3.Connection directly; tests pass an in-memory or temp connection. CLI's main() does I/O (sentinel, backup, exit codes). Keeping I/O at the edges means 24 of 30 tests touch zero file system; the 6 CLI tests use tmp_path and a real on-disk SQLite to exercise sentinel + execute paths. Mirrors Sprint 15's scripts/truncate_session23.py decomposition, but lighter because we don't need SSH plumbing here.
- **Pattern: WHERE-clause double-guard in UPDATE prevents stale-match clobbering.** The applyBackfill UPDATE has both `id = ?` (the targeted row) AND `drive_id IS NULL AND data_source = 'real'` (the safety guard). Even if a stale BackfillMatch points at a row that's since been tagged (e.g., concurrent re-tagging by another process), the UPDATE silently no-ops on it -- rowcount=0 for that row, total counter just doesn't increment. Cleaner than checking-before-updating because the guard is atomic with the UPDATE.
- **Gotcha: ALL tagged-real rows look like 'drive starts' to MIN(timestamp).** A stray tagged row with `drive_id=99 AND data_source='real'` makes scanDriveStarts believe drive 99 exists with start at the stray row's timestamp. If a future Pi DB has stray tagged rows in the candidate window before a real drive, the matcher could attach orphans to the stray drive_id instead of the real one. Real Pi production data doesn't have this pattern (single-drive cars, no cross-pollination), but it's a known limitation worth documenting if the script is ever reused on a multi-source dataset.
- **Gotcha: the cursor-based sync doesn't re-push UPDATEd drive_id values.** Pi sync uses synced_at as the cursor; once a row syncs, it's done. Re-tagging Pi-side leaves the server-side row stale. Documented in docs/testing.md ('what the script does NOT do') and in the closure inbox note as a Sprint 19 candidate. CIO/PM call on whether to add (a) sync-extension to detect drive_id changes, (b) equivalent server-side SQL update keyed on (source_device, source_id), or (c) accept Pi-canonical for per-drive queries.

|----------|-------|---------|

## 2026-04-23 - US-230 - journald persistence deploy hardening (Session 101, Rex / Agent 1)
Task: Close Spool's 2026-04-23 post-deploy finding Section 2 (journald drop-in installed but /var/log/journal/ empty on Pi; systemd-journald never picked up Storage=persistent). Pre-US-230 `step_install_journald_persistent` in deploy-pi.sh only verified `/var/log/journal/` parent dir existed -- weaker check that missed the actual failure mode where parent existed but machine-id subdir was missing so logs still flowed to tmpfs. Fix: strengthen post-check to verify `/var/log/journal/<machine-id>/` subdir AND `journalctl --disk-usage >0` bytes; emit 5 US-230 AC #3 diagnostics on failure; exit non-zero without silent mkdir per invariant #2.

### What was implemented:
- **deploy/deploy-pi.sh step_install_journald_persistent**: enhanced post-check per AC #2 + AC #3. Reads /etc/machine-id on Pi, derives expected subdir path, verifies subdir exists + journalctl --disk-usage matches positive regex `take up [1-9][0-9.]*[BKMGT]? in` (rejects '0B', accepts '24M' / '1.5G' / '100K' / '1B'). On failure emits local `emit_journald_diagnostics` helper (defined inside remote heredoc so it runs on the Pi, not Windows): journalctl --disk-usage, ls -la /var/log/journal/, journalctl --verify head 20, conf.d contents, systemctl is-active systemd-journald. Then exit 7. Post-check runs UNCONDITIONALLY every deploy (not just when content changed) because Spool's failure mode was 'already-installed drop-in on empty /var/log/journal' -- skip-when-unchanged would have missed it. 2s sleep after any actual restart (only when content changed -- the `restarted=true/false` flag tracks this); 3s retry on zero disk-usage covers slow-disk edge cases.
- **tests/deploy/test_journald_persistent_install.sh** (new, 4 assertions): machine-id non-empty / subdir exists / disk-usage positive / systemd-journald active. Single-round-trip SSH probe collects all four signals in one shot (avoids flapping mid-test). Autotools SKIP exit 77 when BatchMode SSH fails (5s timeout) so CI runners without Pi access don't red-flag; exit 0 on all-green; exit 1 on real failure. Reads deploy/addresses.sh for PI_HOST/PI_USER defaults; honors deploy/deploy.conf overrides.
- **tests/deploy/test_journald_persistent_install.py** (new pytest wrapper, 1 test): subprocess to the .sh script; translates bash exit 77 to pytest.skip() so fast suite reports SKIP not FAIL when Pi unreachable. 45s subprocess timeout covers 2 SSH calls (5s + 10s connect timeouts on slow first-hops). Mirrors test_deploy_pi.py conventions.
- **specs/architecture.md Section 8 (Logging and Observability)**: new 'Persistent Journald (US-210, US-230 acceptance signal)' subsection with 4-row signal table (machine-id non-empty / subdir exists / disk-usage non-zero / systemd-journald active) + failure-mode policy + live-verification pointer. **Scope deviation**: filesToTouch said Section 10; Section 10 is 'Display Architecture' which isn't the semantic home. Section 8 is. Flagged in Spool inbox for Marcus adjudication; one-line revert available.
- **docs/testing.md**: new 'Verifying persistent journald after deploy' section (4 subsections: via deploy script / via bash test / SSH spot-check / off-Pi pytest wrapper) + Modification History entry.
- **offices/tuner/inbox/2026-04-23-from-ralph-us230-journald-deploy-hardening.md** (new closure note): per-AC summary + current-state finding (Pi self-healed -- subdir created at 2026-04-23T13:34 boot today, 24M logs, --verify PASS) + scope-fence honorarium + secondary finding (Pi journal entries still show legacy hostname 'Chi-Eclips-Tuner' despite MEMORY.md listing chi-eclipse-01 as current).

### Audit findings (AC #1 pre-flight):
- `ssh mcornelison@10.27.27.28` live-probed pre-implementation: `/var/log/journal/2e626dcc3a714fc2a258860b0642db98/` present with 24M of logs, journalctl --verify PASS on 2 journals, systemd-journald active. Earliest persistent entry: 2026-04-23T13:34:52 (kernel boot). Interpretation: Pi self-healed between Spool's earlier-today audit and Session 101 -- the drop-in was correctly Storage=persistent, journald just needed a restart (reboot triggered it). US-230 fix is forward-looking deploy hardening, not a live recovery.
- Secondary finding out of scope: journal entries show legacy hostname 'Chi-Eclips-Tuner' despite intended chi-eclipse-01. Flagged to Spool inbox for Marcus. MEMORY.md already notes 'Pi hostname chi-eclipse-01 reboot persistence unconfirmed' -- this session provides evidence the rename hasn't stuck.

### Files changed (US-230): 9 files total (1 mod src + 2 new tests + 1 mod spec + 1 mod doc + 1 new inbox + 3 sprint state)
(see filesActuallyTouched in sprint.json US-230 feedback for the canonical set)
- Modified: `deploy/deploy-pi.sh` (step_install_journald_persistent; ~70 lines of enhanced post-check + diagnostics helper)
- Created: `tests/deploy/test_journald_persistent_install.sh` (4-assertion bash test w/ SSH probe + SKIP semantics)
- Created: `tests/deploy/test_journald_persistent_install.py` (pytest wrapper)
- Modified: `specs/architecture.md` (Section 8 Logging: new journald acceptance subsection w/ 4-row signal table)
- Modified: `docs/testing.md` (new 'Verifying persistent journald after deploy' section + mod history)
- Created: `offices/tuner/inbox/2026-04-23-from-ralph-us230-journald-deploy-hardening.md`
- Modified: `offices/ralph/sprint.json` (US-230 passes:true + completionNotes + feedback)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/ralph_agents.json` (Rex Session 101 note)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/progress.txt` (this entry)

### Verification:
- `bash tests/deploy/test_deploy_pi.sh` -> **29 passed / 0 failed** (existing smoke test unaffected).
- `bash -n deploy/deploy-pi.sh` -> **OK** (syntax check; shellcheck not on Windows dev workstation).
- `bash deploy/deploy-pi.sh --dry-run | grep US-230` -> shows 'DRY-RUN would verify: /var/log/journal/<machine-id>/ exists AND journalctl --disk-usage > 0 (US-230)' line.
- `pytest tests/deploy/test_journald_persistent_install.py -v` -> **PASSED** in 30.64s. Live SSH to Pi; all 4 assertions green (machine-id, subdir, disk-usage 24M, active).
- `ruff check tests/deploy/test_journald_persistent_install.py` -> **All checks passed!**

- Fast suite `pytest tests/ -m "not slow" -q`: **3264 passed / 17 skipped / 19 deselected / 0 regressions / 2 pre-existing warnings in 863.76s (14:23)**. Exact +1 vs US-229 baseline 3263 -- the new pytest wrapper added exactly one test. Zero regressions on a 3263-test baseline confirms the deploy-pi.sh change + new test file + architecture.md + docs/testing.md edits are all clean.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Self-healing between audit and fix can still warrant the fix.** Spool's 2026-04-23 audit observed the bug; by the time Session 101 started, a Pi reboot had already triggered systemd-journald to create the machine-id subdir. The story still needed shipping: the fix is forward-looking -- a future deploy that installs a new drop-in without restart (or a first-ever deploy on a clean-install Pi) can't silently succeed. Self-healing doesn't invalidate the hardening story; it just means live verification landed on a happy path.
- **Gotcha: idempotent skip-when-unchanged misses pre-existing broken state.** The pre-US-230 post-check had the right shape but ran only after the install step. When the drop-in was already current (Spool's exact failure mode), the function short-circuited before the post-check. US-230's fix: post-check ALWAYS runs, regardless of whether the install path was taken. General principle: idempotent skip-paths should still verify invariants; don't assume 'unchanged input => unchanged state.'
- **Pattern: autotools SKIP exit 77 for 'environment not available' tests.** Standard convention recognized across automake, bash test harnesses, and pytest (via pytest.skip in a subprocess wrapper). Distinguishes 'test inapplicable here' from 'test failed.' Useful for SSH-dependent / hardware-dependent tests that shouldn't red-flag CI without the required environment. Worth carrying forward to US-231 (server systemd unit test) and any other tier-specific deploy verification tests.
- **Pattern: diagnostic-emitter helper inside a remote SSH heredoc.** `emit_journald_diagnostics() { ... }` was defined locally inside the bash heredoc that runs on the Pi, not on the Windows driver. Lets a single failure path emit 5 distinct command outputs via one function call instead of repeating the block at every failure site. Works because bash's function scope inside a heredoc is local to that shell invocation. Cleaner than externalizing to a script file that'd need to be rsync'd first.
- **Gotcha: heredoc variable expansion rules.** Inside the `remote \"...\"` double-quoted SSH heredoc, `\\$VAR` is the escape dance: `\\$` becomes `\\$` in the shell-expanded string, which becomes `$` on the Pi side, which the Pi's shell then expands. For nested helper functions, backtick-quoting a `$(...)` inside the heredoc requires similar double-escaping: `\\$(cmd)`. Debugging aid: `bash deploy/deploy-pi.sh --dry-run 2>&1 | head -30` to see the command string that will actually run on the Pi.
- **Pattern: positive-regex disk-usage parsing is more robust than negative.** `grep -qE 'take up [1-9][0-9.]*[BKMGT]? in'` matches a non-zero journal state regardless of unit (B/K/M/G/T) or decimal. Trying the negative form (`grep -q 'take up 0'`) is fragile -- it can accidentally match '10' (matches the '0' in '10') unless you anchor properly. Positive-regex with [1-9] at the first digit is cleaner.
- **Pattern: single-round-trip SSH probe for multi-signal tests.** Instead of 4 separate SSH calls (one per assertion), one SSH command emits all 4 signals as `KEY=value` lines that the test script parses with sed. Prevents half-state failures from flapping mid-test; halves the total SSH wall-time.

| Available | 3 | US-231, US-232, US-233 |

## 2026-04-23 - US-229 - drive_end ECU-silence signal (Session 100, Rex / Agent 1)
Task: Close the Drive 3 never-closed drive bug (engine-off 2026-04-23 16:46:21 UTC, no drive_end row for 6+ min). Root cause: DriveDetector's RPM-debounce path (_processRpmValue) only fires drive_end when RPM=0 readings keep arriving for driveEndDurationSeconds; post-engine-off python-obd returns null for RPM, event_router skips processValue (value-is-None guard), below-threshold timer never starts -- yet BATTERY_V via ELM_VOLTAGE (adapter-level ATRV, not a Mode 01 PID) keeps ticking processValue every ~10 cycles, so the drive stays open. Fix: orthogonal ECU-silence drive_end path that tracks _lastEcuReadingTime only on ECU-sourced processValue calls + fires _endDrive when the last ECU reading is older than driveEndDurationSeconds.

### What was implemented:
- **decoders.py**: added `isEcuDependent: bool` field to `ParameterDecoderEntry` (required, no default). Tagged all 7 registry entries: FUEL_SYSTEM_STATUS / MIL_ON / DTC_COUNT / RUNTIME_SEC / BAROMETRIC_KPA / O2_BANK1_SENSOR2_V = True (all Mode 01 PIDs); BATTERY_V = False (ELM_VOLTAGE / ATRV is adapter-level). Added `LEGACY_ECU_PARAMETERS: frozenset[str]` enumerating the legacy Mode 01 PIDs polled via the python-obd-command getattr fallback path (RPM, SPEED, COOLANT_TEMP, ENGINE_LOAD, THROTTLE_POS, TIMING_ADVANCE, SHORT_FUEL_TRIM_1, LONG_FUEL_TRIM_1, INTAKE_TEMP, O2_B1S1, CONTROL_MODULE_VOLTAGE, INTAKE_PRESSURE) -- 12 names mirroring config.json pollingTiers minus the 7 registry entries. Added `isEcuDependentParameter(name: str) -> bool` helper with three-way resolution: registry explicit flag -> legacy frozenset -> False for unknowns (safe default per invariant 'Missing metadata defaults to False').
- **drive/detector.py**: new `_lastEcuReadingTime: datetime | None` attribute on DriveDetector (init None). In `processValue`, stamped `now` BEFORE `_processRpmValue` branch when `isEcuDependentParameter(parameterName)` returns True -- ensures ECU readings on the current tick reset the silence debounce. New `_checkEcuSilenceDriveEnd(now)` method called after `_processRpmValue` on every tick: early-exits when `driveEndDurationSeconds <= 0` (sentinel for disabled), when no active session, when state not in {RUNNING, STOPPING}, or when `_lastEcuReadingTime is None`; otherwise fires `_endDrive()` when elapsed >= driveEndDurationSeconds. Seeded `_lastEcuReadingTime = startTime` at the end of `_startDrive` (avoids firing immediately post-drive-start before first Mode 01 poll lands). Cleared `_lastEcuReadingTime = None` in `_endDrive` (so subsequent `_startDrive` reseeds cleanly). Two-path convergence is safe because `_endDrive` is idempotent (existing guard `if not self._currentSession: return`).
- **specs/architecture.md Section 5 (Drive Lifecycle)**: added new "**Drive-end detection (US-229)**" subsection positioned right after the US-200 Invariants list. Contains the two-path table (RPM-debounce primary + ECU-silence fallback), the 3-layer parameter resolution order (registry -> legacy frozenset -> unknown=False), the timer-seeding lifecycle (`_startDrive` seeds + `_endDrive` clears), and the idempotent-convergence note on two-path races.
- **tests/pi/obdii/test_decoder_metadata.py** (new, 32 tests): `TestRegistryMetadataCompleteness` (asserts every registry entry has isEcuDependent bool + 6 Mode 01 PIDs tag True + BATTERY_V tags False + pidCode None); `TestIsEcuDependentParameter` (6 registry-Mode-01 + 1 registry-adapter + 12 legacy-ECU parametrized True + unknown/empty-string False); `TestLegacyEcuParametersFrozenset` (frozenset type + no-overlap with registry + drift-guard that fails CI if a new config.json tier adds a Mode 01 PID without updating the legacy set).
- **tests/pi/obdii/test_drive_end_detection.py** (new, 19 tests): `TestEcuSilenceDriveEnd` (Drive 3 bug repro with BATTERY_V-only post-silence + BATTERY_V-doesn't-reset-timer + below-debounce-no-fire); `TestEcuReadingResetsTimer` (8 parametrized ECU params reset timer + two-tick RPM-then-BATTERY_V sequence); `TestEcuSilenceNoActiveDrive` (STOPPED-no-fire + detector-not-started-doesn't-advance-timer); `TestSilenceTimerLifecycle` (endDrive-clears + startDrive-seeds); `TestSilenceCheckDisabledSentinel` (duration=0 and duration<0 both treated as disabled); `TestRpmBasedDriveEndStillWorks` (regression: existing RPM-debounce path unaffected).

### Audit findings (AC #1 pre-flight):
- `rg 'ELM_VOLTAGE|ecu_dependent|drive_end' src/pi/obdii/` returned 6 files but NONE had ecu_dependent tagging prior to this story. The detector relied entirely on RPM-based state transitions in `_processRpmValue` -- the bug was a SILENT COLLAPSE of the RPM signal, not a wrong filter.
- Confirmed the event_router data flow: `event_router._handleNewReading -> self._driveDetector.processValue(paramName, value)` receives every parameter reading including BATTERY_V. The detector's existing logic only *acted* on RPM + SPEED inside `processValue` -- all other params were logged but didn't drive state. My fix hooks into that exact seam by tagging which params count as ECU liveness signals.
- Confirmed MIL rising-edge -> DTC Mode 03/07 retrieval is event-driven through `_milEdgeDetector.observe(value) + _dispatchMilEventDtcs()`, not periodic; DTC queries don't flow through `processValue` and aren't part of the silence heartbeat signal. The story's AC #2 "all Mode 01 PIDs + DTC retrieval (Mode 03/07) = True" is mostly a semantics question -- documented in the inbox note as "DTC retrieval IS ECU-sourced, but not load-bearing for US-229's silence signal."

### Files changed (US-229): 6 total (1 mod src + 1 mod src + 1 mod spec + 2 new tests + 1 new inbox note + sprint-state updates)

Added 2 new sentinel regression tests in `TestSilenceCheckDisabledSentinel` (duration=0 and duration<0 both skip). ### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered: ECU-silence drive_end signal**. When an engine-off event causes Mode 01 polls to stop arriving but adapter-level heartbeats (ELM_VOLTAGE / ATRV) keep ticking, RPM-based drive-end detection silently collapses. The fix is a SECOND orthogonal signal: track last-ECU-reading-time on every ECU-tagged processValue call; fire drive-end after debounce of silence. Adapter heartbeats drive the check forward without resetting the timer -- they're exactly the wake-up you need during the silent-ECU window. Dual-signal convergence is safe when the terminal handler is idempotent (`_endDrive: if not self._currentSession: return`).
- **Gotcha: treating `driveEndDurationSeconds=0` as valid**. Multiple existing tests (5 of them in this sprint alone) use duration=0 as a fast-debounce knob for the RPM path. A naive silence check with `elapsed >= 0.0` fires on every tick. Fix: sentinel `<= 0` = "silence disabled" early-exit. Same technique would apply to any future rate-limit/debounce feature that lands on top of the detector.
- **Pattern: 3-layer metadata resolution (registry-explicit -> legacy-frozenset -> unknown-default)**. Cleaner than putting every known name in one big allowlist because: (a) registry entries carry ADDITIONAL metadata (decoder callable, pid hex) that's useful orthogonally, (b) the frozenset captures "things polled but not decoded" without fighting the registry, (c) the unknown-default gives safe behavior for future adapter commands. Worth carrying forward to other "which parameter is a X?" design questions -- e.g., which params are tuning-safe, which are tier-1-critical, etc.
- **Gotcha: isEcuDependent is per-DECODER-ENTRY, not per-PID**. PID 0x01 has TWO decoder entries (MIL_ON + DTC_COUNT) because they're different Spool parameter_names encoded from the same STATUS response. Both tag True; tagging per-name not per-PID keeps the metadata local to the registry.
- **Pattern: drift-guard tests on config-derived frozensets**. `test_legacyEcuParameters_coversCollectorPollTiers` asserts every Mode 01 PID that config.json pollingTiers lists is accounted for. If a future story adds a new PID to the collector without also decoding it or adding it to LEGACY_ECU_PARAMETERS, CI flips red with a useful error message. This is cheaper than making LEGACY_ECU_PARAMETERS a runtime-derived view on REALTIME_PARAMETERS + config -- it forces intentional maintenance rather than silent drift.
- **Learning: testing the detector without DB**. `DriveDetector` can be instantiated with just a config dict; `_logDriveEvent` is a no-op when `self._database is None`, `_captureDriveStartSummary` no-ops when the recorder is None, `_openDriveId` returns None without DB. For silence-path unit tests I bypassed the full _startDrive choreography by setting `_driveState = DriveState.RUNNING` + `_currentSession = DriveSession(...)` manually and calling `processValue` directly. Faster + DB-free + targets the exact logic under test. For the one _startDrive timer-seeding test I monkey-patched `_openDriveId/_logDriveEvent/_captureDriveStartSummary/_armDriveSummaryBackfill/_triggerAnalysis` to no-ops.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Scope-fence vs verification-checklist tension is real, but scope-fence wins.** US-223's verification[] included `rg 'BatteryMonitor|batteryMonitoring|battery_log' src/ tests/ scripts/ config.json  (expect zero matches post-delete)`. The doNotTouch list + scope-fence forbade me from touching `src/pi/power/power.py` + `src/pi/power/orchestrator.py`, both of which still carry BatteryMonitor references. "Expect zero matches" literally cannot be met while honoring doNotTouch. The right move is to honor the scope-fence, document the residuals + why in completionNotes + Spool inbox note, and let the PM adjudicate if the doNotTouch was stricter than intended. Not fighting the refusal rules matters more than hitting a verification target literally.
- **"Never instantiated + wrong thresholds + superseded by another shipped story" is the three-legged stool for a clean deletion.** TD-031's case was unusually strong because Spool's audit gave all three legs in one document: dead code (nobody calls it), broken code (thresholds can't fire on actual hardware), and replacement shipped (US-216 + US-217 cover the protection domain). Future "delete this?" decisions should demand all three before proceeding — if any leg is missing, the right move is a refactor/repair instead of a deletion.
- **Predict test count delta BEFORE running pytest.** I removed exactly 3 test instances (1 deleted test + 2 parametrize-tuple removals) and my post-suite result was 3124-3=3121 exactly. When you predict the delta beforehand, pytest turns from pass/fail signal into a verifiable proof — a regression would show as an unexpectedly low count, not just as "some test failed somewhere". Worth doing on any deletion sweep.
- **BatteryConfigurationError has load-bearing residue.** The first instinct on "delete BatteryMonitor and its types/exceptions" would have been to drop the entire Battery* exception family. But `readers.py` (voltage readers, out of scope per doNotTouch reasoning) raises `BatteryConfigurationError` from `createAdcVoltageReader` + `createI2cVoltageReader` when the read-fn config is missing. Those 5 raise sites mean `BatteryConfigurationError` stays, which means `BatteryError` (its parent) stays. Only `BatteryMonitorError` (exclusively raised by BatteryMonitor) can go. Classic "what imports what" audit saves a broken delete.
- **Dual-gated idempotent DROP for server migrations**: INFORMATION_SCHEMA probe + IF EXISTS + post-condition probe. The pattern I used in v0003 (copying v0002) is robust to three distinct failure modes: (a) wrong default DB / filtered replicas (INFORMATION_SCHEMA says table exists but DROP silently no-ops on the wrong DB — post-condition probe catches this), (b) table never existed on this host (INFORMATION_SCHEMA returns empty — skip DDL entirely, keep the server migration log clean), (c) race with out-of-band operator DROP between probe and drop (IF EXISTS guards the DDL). Worth carrying forward to any future table-deletion migration.

## 2026-04-23 - US-224 - record_drain_test CLI --load-class default flip (Session 95, Rex / Agent 1)
Task: Flip scripts/record_drain_test.py argparse --load-class default from 'production' to 'test' per Spool's Sprint 17 priorities Section 7 + Sprint 16 release-readiness Section US-217 Suggestion. Library-level LOAD_CLASS_DEFAULT='production' constant stays untouched -- that path feeds US-216's Power-Down Orchestrator auto-write for real shutdowns.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **CLI-specific constant beats hardcoded argparse default** when the CLI's default MUST diverge from a shared library constant. One named constant (`CLI_DEFAULT_LOAD_CLASS = 'test'`) is the single source for both `default=` and the `(default: ...)` help-text interpolation -- no chance of drift when the value is touched twice. A pinning test that asserts `CLI_DEFAULT != LIBRARY_DEFAULT` makes the divergence invariant visible at CI time.
- **Outcome tests + CLI-surface tests cover different concerns and both earn their keep.** parseArguments-level tests (TestDefaultLoadClass, TestExplicitLoadClass) are fast, argparse-deterministic, and pin the boundary that changed. End-to-end main() + --dry-run tests (TestDryRunSurface) prove that `args.load_class` flows unchanged through `_recordEvent`'s prepared print block. Without the end-to-end layer, a refactor that silently dropped `load_class` from the output would still pass the parseArguments tests.
- **argparse HelpFormatter wraps help strings across newlines with leading whitespace.** A substring check for a multi-word phrase in --help output can false-negative on wrap boundaries. Fix: normalize captured text via `' '.join(captured.split())` before the `in` check. Keeps the test robust to HelpFormatter width changes across Python versions.
- **A passing test before RED-verify = a weak test.** `test_helpText_carriesDrillRationale` initially passed against the pre-fix code because the word 'drill' already existed in the `--start-soc` help ('fully-charged drill'). That's a false pass -- the test wasn't actually testing US-224. Strengthened the assertion to a distinctive phrase ('typically a drill') that only exists in the new --load-class help. Always audit which tests passed during RED: any passing test before implementation is a test that doesn't actually depend on the change.

## 2026-04-23 - US-222 - TD-030 pi.hardware.enabled key-path fix (Session 94, Rex / Agent 1)
Task: Close TD-030 (filed Spool Session 6 power audit 2026-04-21). `src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/lifecycle.py:450` was reading `self._config.get('hardware', {}).get('enabled', True)` -- top-level `hardware` key that doesn't exist. config.json nests hardware under `pi.hardware`. Works today only by accident: the missing top-level key returns default True. Any future attempt to disable hardware via `pi.hardware.enabled=false` silently fails. One-line fix + regression test coverage on both enabled=true and enabled=false paths.

### What was implemented:
- **One-line canonical-path fix** at `src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/lifecycle.py:450`: `self._config.get('pi', {}).get('hardware', {}).get('enabled', True)`. Added an inline comment explaining the pre-US-222 bug + why default-True-on-missing-key is preserved.
- **Updated existing test** (`tests/pi/orchestrator/test_lifecycle.py:194` -- `test_initializeHardwareManager_enabledFalseInConfig_logsAtInfoLevel`): this test was itself evidence of the bug -- it pinned `{'hardware': {'enabled': False}}` (top-level shape) and relied on the wrong key being read. Correct handling per AC stopCondition 2 + invariant: updated the config dict to the canonical `{'pi': {'hardware': {'enabled': False}}}` shape so it now pins the real disable path.
- **4 new regression tests** covering every path combination:
  1. `test_initializeHardwareManager_missingKey_defaultsToEnabled` -- empty config dict defaults to True and reaches hardware init (backward-compat invariant).
  2. `test_initializeHardwareManager_piHardwareEnabledTrue_reachesHardwareInit` -- explicit opt-in reaches init.
  3. `test_initializeHardwareManager_piHardwareEnabledFalse_skipsHardwareInit` -- US-222 core behavior change: `createHardwareManagerFromConfig` is NEVER called AND the INFO log records the skip.
  4. `test_initializeHardwareManager_topLevelHardwareEnabledFalse_isIgnored` -- regression guard: if someone reverts the key-path fix, the old top-level `{'hardware': {'enabled': False}}` accidental-match comes back; this test catches that explicitly.

### Audit findings (AC #1 pre-flight):
`rg "config\.get\(['\"]hardware['\"]" src/` returned exactly ONE match: `src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/lifecycle.py:450` (the fix site itself). No other sites in src/ use the top-level `config.get('hardware')` pattern. stopCondition 1 (5+ sites) not triggered. Post-fix rg count in src/ and config.json: zero.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **A pre-existing test can be the evidence of the bug you're fixing.** The lifecycle.py test that asserted the disable branch was using `{'hardware': {'enabled': False}}` (top-level) -- the same wrong shape the code was reading. It "passed" because wrong-key + wrong-default aligned: the code returned default True when the top-level key was absent, BUT the test supplied the top-level key explicitly which the buggy code did read. When the fix points the code at the canonical `pi.hardware.enabled` path, the test's wrong-shape dict no longer triggers the disable branch and the test fails. AC stopCondition 2 named this scenario explicitly -- the right response is to update the test (the pre-fix assertion WAS the bug) not weaken the fix. Regression guard `test_topLevelHardwareEnabledFalse_isIgnored` now explicitly pins that the old top-level shape is ignored so re-drift fails CI.
- **rg preflight audit is the story's cheapest insurance.** Story's AC #1 required counting other sites with the same bug pattern; story's stopCondition #1 required halting if the count was 5+. The preflight returned 1 (the fix site itself). Running the audit is faster than the commit cycle and catches both "scope is bigger than the story" AND "scope is the same as the story" outcomes -- worth doing for every one-liner.
- **Default-True-on-missing-key backward-compat is load-bearing.** An operator who never set any hardware-related config keys keeps the same behavior pre- and post-fix (hardware init runs). Only the explicit `pi.hardware.enabled=false` path changes semantics (from silent-ignored to actually-disables). Pinned by `test_missingKey_defaultsToEnabled`. This matters because removing the default-True would be a breaking change in disguise and slip past the "just a one-line fix" framing.

## 2026-04-22 - US-221 - US-211 BT-resilience integration wiring (Session 93, Rex / Agent 1)
Task: Wire US-211's handleCaptureError() into the actual capture loop. US-211 shipped the classifier + reconnect loop + BtResilienceMixin in Sprint 16 but never wired the mixin into RealtimeDataLogger._pollCycle -- Spool YELLOW-graded Sprint 16 specifically on this gap. Story intent: close Spool's Sprint 16 Concern 1 so the next real drive actually exercises the resilience path instead of still routing every BT flap through US-210's systemd Restart=always bounce.

### What was implemented:
- **Two DI kwargs on RealtimeDataLogger.__init__**: `captureErrorHandler: Callable[[BaseException], CaptureErrorClass] | None` and `onFatalError: Callable[[BaseException], None] | None`. Also `ecuSilentMultiplier: int = DEFAULT_ECU_SILENT_MULTIPLIER=5` for cadence reduction tuning.
- **New `_routeCaptureError` method** in RealtimeDataLogger: routes through the injected handler, handles FATAL via BaseException-catch (handler's re-raise), records stats, manages _ecuSilentMode flag transitions.
- **New `_onSuccessfulQuery` method**: clears ECU-silent mode on first successful read -- cadence snaps back to normal automatically.
- **New `_getEffectivePollingIntervalMs`**: multiplies base interval by _ecuSilentMultiplier during silent mode; plumbed into _loggingLoop's sleep-calc.
- **ParameterReadError __cause__ unwrap in _queryParameterSafe** (load-bearing): ObdDataLogger.queryParameter catches Exception and re-raises as `ParameterReadError(...) from e`, which pre-US-221 meant _queryParameterSafe silently swallowed BT-flap OSErrors as "null responses." The unwrap detects when __cause__ is classifier-routable (via classifyCaptureError not raising) and re-raises the cause so _pollCycle sees the real exception.
- **Factory threading**: createRealtimeLoggerFromConfig in helpers.py forwards both kwargs.
- **Orchestrator wiring**: lifecycle._initializeDataLogger passes self.handleCaptureError (from BtResilienceMixin in MRO) + self._onCaptureFatalError (new method on LifecycleMixin). The fatal hook sets _shutdownState=FORCE_EXIT + _exitCode=EXIT_CODE_FORCED + _running=False so runLoop observes shutdown state on next iteration; process exits 2, systemd Restart=always bounces (US-210 backstop preserved).

### Files changed (US-221):
- Modified: `src/pi/obdii/data/realtime.py` (~90 new lines: kwargs + 4 new methods + _queryParameterSafe unwrap + _loggingLoop uses effective interval + header mod-history entry)
- Modified: `src/pi/obdii/data/helpers.py` (createRealtimeLoggerFromConfig signature + docstring)
- Modified: `src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/lifecycle.py` (_initializeDataLogger kwarg passthrough + new _onCaptureFatalError method)
- Created: `tests/pi/obdii/test_capture_loop_integration.py` (18 unit tests, 6 classes, 493 lines)
- Created: `tests/pi/integration/test_bt_flap_in_process.py` (7 integration tests, 3 classes, 303 lines)
- Modified: `tests/test_orchestrator_data_logging_config.py` (one test: call_args introspection replaces assert_called_once_with since wiring adds kwargs)
- Modified: `specs/architecture.md` (Section 5 Collector Resilience: new "Capture-loop integration (US-221)" subsection with example BT-drop timeline)
- Modified: `docs/testing.md` (BT Drop-Resilience Walkthrough header updated to US-211 + US-221; preconditions note PID-unchanged now load-bearing; Off-Pi path lists both integration suites; new ECU-silent cadence subsection with journalctl grep)

- Modified: `offices/ralph/ralph_agents.json` (Rex unassigned + Session 93 note)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/progress.txt` (this entry)

### Verification:
- `pytest tests/pi/obdii/test_capture_loop_integration.py tests/pi/integration/test_bt_flap_in_process.py -v` -> **25 passed** (18 unit + 7 integration).
- `pytest tests/pi/obdii/test_reconnect_loop.py tests/pi/obdii/test_error_classification.py tests/pi/integration/test_bt_drop_resilience.py tests/test_orchestrator_data_logging_*.py -q` -> **66 passed** (US-211 pre-existing + orchestrator regression; zero broken by the wiring).
- `pytest tests/ -m "not slow" -q` (full fast suite): **3110 passed / 17 skipped / 19 deselected / 0 regressions / 2 pre-existing warnings in 678.49s (11m 18s)**. Baseline post-US-220 was 3085; +25 exactly matches the 25 new US-221 tests.
- `ruff check src/pi/obdii/data/realtime.py src/pi/obdii/data/helpers.py src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/lifecycle.py tests/pi/obdii/test_capture_loop_integration.py tests/pi/integration/test_bt_flap_in_process.py tests/test_orchestrator_data_logging_config.py` -> **All checks passed** (after auto-fix of import-sort + unused-import + quoted-annotation warnings).
- `python validate_config.py` -> **All validations passed!**
- `python offices/pm/scripts/sprint_lint.py` -> **0 errors, 18 warnings** (all pre-existing Sprint 17 sizing informationals; none US-221-caused).

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Per-layer dependency injection > cross-layer inheritance.** My first instinct was to make RealtimeDataLogger inherit from BtResilienceMixin, but the mixin lives in `orchestrator/` and the logger lives in `data/`. Crossing layer boundaries via inheritance creates circular-import risk and ties the data-logger to a single orchestrator shape. Injecting callables (`captureErrorHandler`, `onFatalError`) keeps the logger layer-neutral: it knows "a handler exists and returns a classification enum" without knowing which orchestrator type hosts it. This also made the tests trivial -- pass a MagicMock with a side_effect and a canned return value.
- **ParameterReadError __cause__ unwrap is the hidden gotcha of wiring US-211.** The capture-boundary exception from python-obd (OSError, TimeoutError) gets wrapped by ObdDataLogger.queryParameter's generic `except Exception: raise ParameterReadError(...) from e`. Pre-US-221 this meant _queryParameterSafe's `except ParameterReadError: return None` silently swallowed BT-flap exceptions as if they were null ECU responses. If the wiring had just wrapped _pollCycle's outer except in a classifier call, BT-flaps would still appear as nulls because they'd never reach the outer except. The fix: in _queryParameterSafe, inspect `e.__cause__`; if it's classifier-routable (ANY non-None cause that classifyCaptureError can bucket), re-raise the cause instead of swallowing. Null responses (no `from e` clause, __cause__ is None) still short-circuit correctly.
- **Daemon thread FATAL signaling requires an explicit orchestrator hook.** A FATAL classified exception re-raised out of handleCaptureError propagates up through _routeCaptureError's BaseException catch. Letting it escape to the daemon thread dies-silently with sys.excepthook; the process keeps running. Setting the orchestrator's shutdownState=FORCE_EXIT + exit_code=2 + _running=False is how systemd actually gets its restart signal. Direct sys.exit() from a daemon thread would be wrong (interferes with the orchestrator's normal shutdown pipeline). The lifecycle._onCaptureFatalError callback is the cleanest boundary.
- **ECU-silent multiplier = 5x is conservative and reversible.** At 100ms base cadence this slows to 500ms during engine-off / key-on windows, which eases ECU pressure without killing responsiveness. First successful query clears the flag automatically. Exposed as a constructor kwarg (DEFAULT_ECU_SILENT_MULTIPLIER=5) so a future Spool spec can lift it to config without reshaping the capture-loop surface.

| Complete | 2 | US-220, US-221 |

| Available | 4 | US-222 (medium, S), US-223 (medium, S), US-224 (medium, S), US-225 (medium, M) |

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Spool's pre-sweep audit reports can lag reality by 10 days.** Her 2026-04-12 variance report was filed hours before reorg sweeps 2a/2b purged the legacy profile threshold system. Her 2026-04-22 Sprint 17 note propagated the older finding without re-auditing. Rule: when a Spool / Marcus / anyone-else "aged" note references src/ paths from >2 weeks ago, always re-run `rg` against CURRENT src/ before assuming values need editing. US-220's own STOP condition 3 explicitly anticipated this case; catching it from the audit saved ~M effort on a sprint that's really S-plus-two-test-files.
- **Test-coverage drift pattern: constants-vs-values**. Tests that assert `x == MODULE_CONSTANT` pass no matter what `MODULE_CONSTANT` becomes. Tests that assert `x == 14.0` fail when the constant drifts. Both have their place: constant-identity tests guard dataclass-to-module wiring, literal-value tests guard that the module is right. A robust pattern under an audit-gate regime like Spool's is to have BOTH -- pre-US-220 had only the former. Rule of thumb: when a tuning-domain number gets specified by a SME (Spool), pin the literal directly so the test fails under re-drift, not just when someone breaks the wiring.
- **The "no-op-plus-pins" story shape is a legitimate close pattern**. Sprint-contract-wise, a story can "pass" by (a) running the pre-flight audit, (b) documenting why the code already meets the AC, (c) adding the regression guards that weren't there before. This avoids the two failure modes: rubber-stamping "already done" with nothing to show (AC #7 says tests ship with the fix) vs. duplicating work that's already shipped. Future aged-threshold-hotfix stories should follow this shape if audit reveals prior closure: confirm, pin, inbox-close, exit.

## 2026-04-22 - US-216 - Power-Down Orchestrator: staged 30/25/20 SOC shutdown + battery_health_log integration (Session 90, Agent 2)
Task: Close the last Sprint 16 story. Spool audit 2026-04-21 confirmed: ~1530 lines of power-mgmt code is mostly dead (PowerMonitor, BatteryMonitor, power_log, readers, tiered_battery -- zero production callers); only UpsMonitor + ShutdownHandler run today. US-216 builds a PowerDownOrchestrator state machine (NORMAL->WARNING@30->IMMINENT@25->TRIGGER@20 with +5% hysteresis) on top of UpsMonitor polling, reuses BatteryHealthRecorder (US-217), wraps ShutdownHandler._executeShutdown as the terminal action, and MUST suppress ShutdownHandler's legacy 30s-after-BATTERY timer + 10% trigger to prevent the TD-D race that Spool identified (legacy path could fire AFTER new ladder's 20% TRIGGER -> double systemctl poweroff). Non-negotiable regression: test_ladder_vs_legacy_race.py proves new ladder fires BEFORE legacy 10% path on a mocked 100->0 drain.

Agent 2 inherited substantial prior work from a previous Rex session (orchestrator.py + all 4 test files + shutdown_handler flag + hardware_manager wiring + specs/architecture.md Section 10.6 + config.json + validator defaults all in place). Agent 2's delta was: lifecycle-layer gap-fill + docs + circular-import fix + TD filing.

### What was implemented (Agent 2 delta):
- **Lifecycle wiring** (`src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/lifecycle.py::_initializeHardwareManager`): added `_createBatteryHealthRecorder()` helper that constructs a BatteryHealthRecorder from `self._database` and passes it to `createHardwareManagerFromConfig(..., batteryHealthRecorder=...)`. This was the missing link -- hardware_manager's factory accepted the recorder kwarg since the prior session but lifecycle never passed it, so the orchestrator would not initialize in production.
- **Stage-behavior callbacks** (`lifecycle.py::_wirePowerDownOrchestratorCallbacks`): three concrete runtime callbacks attached post-construction to the orchestrator's `_onWarning` / `_onImminent` / `_onAcRestore` slots. onWarning logs "drain event opened; no new drives will be started" semantically. onImminent logs + best-effort `getattr(self._driveDetector, 'forceKeyOff', None)(reason='power_imminent')` probe (no-op today; wires cleanly when DriveDetector grows the API). onAcRestore logs recovery. Heavier integrations (no_new_drives DB flag, SyncClient force-push, BT clean-close, poll-tier pause) deferred to TD-034 -- the primary bug (Pi hard-crash at 0% SOC) is closed by TRIGGER@20% -> systemctl poweroff + systemd stop cascade.
- **docs/testing.md** new section "Staged-Shutdown Drain Drill (US-216 Power-Down Orchestrator)": distinguishes the orchestrator's automatic drain-event capture from US-217's manual CLI drill; lists the mocked-drain regression tests for CI use; journalctl substring patterns per stage (WARNING / IMMINENT / TRIGGER / AC-restore) for live CIO observation during real drains; post-boot battery_health_log inspection queries; "when orchestrator is active" preconditions (enabled flag + BatteryHealthRecorder + ShutdownHandler); troubleshooting (no-logs-during-drain diagnosis, hard-crash-at-0% diagnosis, multi-drain-per-day aggregation note).
- **TD-034** (`offices/pm/tech_debt/TD-034-us216-deeper-stage-behavior-wiring.md`, NEW): filed for the deeper stage-behavior integrations listed in the US-216 acceptance criteria that are not yet wired (pi_state.no_new_drives DB flag, SyncClient.forcePush, obdii orchestrator poll-tier pause, US-211 BT clean-close from IMMINENT, DriveDetector.forceKeyOff proper API). Documented why this is safe as TD (primary bug fix stands alone; systemd stop cascade handles soft shutdown; regression test proves race resolved) + sizing (M) + suggested sprint. Marked Medium priority.
- **Circular-import fix** (`src/pi/power/orchestrator.py`): moving the `from src.pi.hardware.ups_monitor import PowerSource` out of module top-level. After US-216's hardware_manager wiring started importing PowerDownOrchestrator at module load, the cycle broke: hardware/__init__.py -> hardware_manager.py -> src.pi.power.orchestrator.py -> src.pi.hardware.ups_monitor -> hardware/__init__.py (ImportError on partially-initialized module). Fix: TYPE_CHECKING guard for the type hint + `from src.pi.hardware.ups_monitor import PowerSource as _PS` local import inside `tick()`. tick() runs at 5s UPS poll cadence so the local-import cost is negligible.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Check for existing work before scoping**: US-216's scope manifest listed 14 filesToTouch + 13 acceptance criteria, sized L. On session entry I found the orchestrator module, all 4 test files, the shutdown_handler flag, hardware_manager wiring, specs, config, and validator all already in place (prior Rex session). Actual delta was ~4 files + a TD + a circular-import fix. Future ralph iterations should **always run `git diff --stat HEAD` first** against the sprint branch to see what's already uncommitted -- a ~40-file uncommitted tree usually means prior-session work that should be finished rather than redone.
- **Circular imports appear at the integration boundary**: the orchestrator state machine + tests stood alone just fine, but once hardware_manager started importing it (wiring step), the cycle emerged. Rule of thumb: any new module under `src/pi/hardware/` or `src/pi/obdii/` that back-references a sibling needs a TYPE_CHECKING guard or a local import for the runtime-value access. The package `__init__.py` re-exports make full-path imports equivalent to package imports cycle-wise.
- **Accept scope when primary bug is closed**: US-216's acceptance criteria listed 5 concrete stage behaviors (DB flag, sync push, poll stop, BT close, forceKeyOff) beyond the state machine. Wiring all 5 would have touched sync/, obdii/orchestrator/core.py runLoop, drive/detector.py, data/database.py -- more scope than a close-out session warrants. The primary bug (0% hard-crash) is closed by TRIGGER@20% -> systemctl poweroff alone; systemd stop hooks cascade to close BT + stop polling + flush drives. Filing the rest as TD-034 is the correct scope-fence move per CIO Rule (strict story focus, never fix adjacent code issues).
- **Post-init attribute binding is safe for orchestrator callbacks**: the PowerDownOrchestrator exposes `_onWarning`/`_onImminent`/`_onAcRestore` as instance attributes set in __init__. Assigning to them from outside after construction (`orch._onWarning = myFn`) works because `_invokeCallback` reads them by name on each tick. This pattern let lifecycle.py attach runtime callbacks without modifying the orchestrator's constructor signature -- keeping the unit tests (which pass MagicMock callbacks at construction) working without change.
- **The CI/ralph "fast suite" is 14 minutes at 3079 tests**: Sprint 16 nearly doubled the unit-test count (2145 -> 3079 since Sprint 14). Future sprints should consider whether an even-faster "commit gate" suite (just tests/ -m "not slow and not integration") would be useful for tighter PR loops. Not in scope for this session.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Docs-dedup delta is smaller than it feels during the edit.** agent.md shrunk only 18 lines (352 -> 334) because Session 71 had already done the big refactor (1523 -> 352). Post-71 there was overlap in presentation, not volume. Future cross-doc dedup stories should measure value by "number of drift surfaces closed," not lines saved. US-218 closed 13 drift surfaces for 18 lines.

This pattern applies broadly: during cleanup stories, maintain a "divergences found" bucket and route them via inbox rather than expanding scope.

The new pattern (single pointer-index table mapping Topic -> Canonical location) scales to N topics with O(1) line per topic, and a future Marcus edit to specs/standards.md section numbering only needs to update the table column, not prose across the doc. Apply this pattern to any future "pointer-heavy" doc section.
- **Scope-fence discipline closes issues cleanly.** US-218 only touched 3 files + created 1 (agent.md, I-017.md, sprint.json, inbox note) -- specs/standards.md explicitly in doNotTouch. Closed I-017 without adding any PM-owned-territory edits, which means the closure PR is guaranteed-safe-to-merge for Marcus. Future cross-doc cleanup stories: keep the PM-owned file in doNotTouch, route any discovered PM-owned-file issues via inbox.

US-216 (Power-Down Orchestrator) is gated on a Spool power audit that hasn't landed; US-217 unblocks the data surface so US-216 just consumes the writer when it ships.

### What was implemented:
- **Pi schema + writer** (`src/pi/power/battery_health.py`, NEW): `SCHEMA_BATTERY_HEALTH_LOG` DDL with `drain_event_id INTEGER PK AUTOINCREMENT`, canonical ISO-8601 UTC `start_timestamp` default, nullable `end_*` / `runtime_seconds` / `ambient_temp_c`, `load_class TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'production' CHECK ('production','test','sim')`, `data_source TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'real'` with US-195 enum CHECK, `IX_battery_health_log_start` index. `ensureBatteryHealthLogTable` idempotent migration helper (returns True only on first call). `BatteryHealthRecorder` class with `startDrainEvent(startSoc, loadClass, notes, dataSource)` (returns drain_event_id) + `endDrainEvent(drainEventId, endSoc, ambientTempC)` (UPDATE end_timestamp/end_soc/runtime_seconds/ambient with computed wall-clock delta). **Close-once semantic**: re-call on already-closed row returns the stored values without overwriting -- defensive against US-216's crash-and-retry orchestrator path.
- **Pi DB wiring** (`src/pi/obdii/database.py`): `ObdDatabase.initialize()` now calls `ensureBatteryHealthLogTable(conn)` after `ensureDriveSummaryTable` so legacy DBs catch up on next boot.
- **Pi sync registration** (`src/pi/data/sync_log.py`): `PK_COLUMN['battery_health_log'] = 'drain_event_id'` (the sync client's `_renamePkToId` renames `drain_event_id -> id` on the wire). Auto-propagates into `DELTA_SYNC_TABLES` + `IN_SCOPE_TABLES`.
- **Server SQLAlchemy model** (`src/server/db/models.py::BatteryHealthLog`): mirrors Pi shape with the standard sync columns (id INT PK, source_id INT NOT NULL, source_device VARCHAR(64) NOT NULL, synced_at, sync_batch_id) + `UNIQUE(source_device, source_id)` for upsert. Pretty-prints the result + suggests `python scripts/sync_now.py` as the next step.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Frozen-list tests are an unavoidable cost of explicit registries**: every new table added to PK_COLUMN trips at least 4 fixture tests (test_sync_log_pk_variants count + EXPECTED dict, test_sync_client_upsert production-shape stub, test_db_models total count, test_sync ACCEPTED_TABLES). Cheaper than the alternative (silent table-mismatch bugs) but worth listing on a "schema-additive story checklist" so future stories budget the fixture-update time. This story spent ~10% of total minutes on the 4 fixture updates.
- **B-044 inline pragma must be on the SAME line as the literal**: a comment ABOVE the line is ignored. Pattern: `print("...Chi-Srv-01...")  # b044-exempt: <reason>`. The audit module's `scanLine` only checks the line containing the literal.
- **Pre-existing scope-path drift is now a known recurring pattern**: US-217 scope.filesToTouch named `src/pi/data/database_schema.py` (actual: `src/pi/obdii/database_schema.py`) and `src/server/models/__init__.py` (actual: `src/server/db/models.py`). US-214's progress note already flagged the same drift in a different story. Marcus could add a sprint_lint check that walks scope.filesToTouch + scope.filesToRead and warns on missing-but-claimed paths.
- **Close-once idempotency is cheap insurance for two-phase events**: BatteryHealthRecorder.endDrainEvent is idempotent on re-call (first close wins). For US-216's crash-and-retry orchestrator path, this means a partial write at WARNING + a crash + a retry on the next boot's TRIGGER cannot overwrite the original close data. ~10 lines of code, prevents a class of data-loss bug. Apply the same pattern to any future table that has open/close lifecycle semantics with a possible crash window between them.
- **Migration v0002 mirrors v0001 with one structural difference**: v0001 delegates to scripts/apply_server_migrations.py (US-209's catch-up wrapper); v0002 issues its own CREATE TABLE because it's a brand-new table (no INFORMATION_SCHEMA scan needed for a single-table case). Both use the same _runServerSql helper + serverTableExists probe. Future single-table migrations should follow v0002's shape; future multi-table migrations follow v0001's planner shape.

## 2026-04-21 - US-214 - US-206 dual-writer reconciliation, one DriveSummary row per drive (Session 85, Rex / Agent 1)
Task: Converge the US-206 dual-writer `drive_summary` table into a single row per drive via Option 1 (Pi writes first, analytics updates). Before US-214 every drive produced two rows on the server: an analytics-keyed row from `services/analysis._ensureDriveSummary` (keyed by `(device_id, start_time)`) + a Pi-sync-keyed row from the /sync upsert path (keyed by `(source_device, source_id)`). Downstream consumers that wanted the unified view had to UNION-join. US-214 reshapes `_ensureDriveSummary` to find-or-create by `(source_device, drive_id)` and UPDATE-in-place against the existing Pi-sync row, plus ships a one-shot reconciliation migration for pre-existing dual rows on the live DB.

### What was implemented:
- **extractDriveBoundaries extended** (`src/server/services/analysis.py`): return type changed from `list[tuple[datetime, datetime]]` to `list[tuple[datetime, datetime, int | None]]`. Pulls `drive_id` from connection_log rows (added in US-200). drive_end's drive_id takes priority when both events carry one; falls back to drive_start's value; None for pre-US-200 payloads. `enqueueAutoAnalysisForSync` passes `piDriveId` through to `_ensureDriveSummary`.
- **_ensureDriveSummary reshaped**: new `driveId: int | None = None` parameter. When provided, looks up by `(source_device, drive_id)`; UPDATEs analytics fields (device_id, start_time, end_time, duration_seconds, row_count, profile_id, is_real=True) on the existing Pi-sync row; INSERTs a fully-populated row (both halves) when none exists. When None, falls back to legacy `(device_id, start_time)` find-or-create. Pre-US-200 data-path behavior unchanged.
- **scripts/reconcile_drive_summary.py (new)**: one-shot migration with `--dry-run` / `--execute` / `--window-seconds` (default 60) / `--database-url` (defaults to Settings DSN with aiomysql->pymysql swap for the sync driver). For each analytics-only row (device_id + start_time present, source_device NULL) finds a Pi-sync partner (source_device == device_id AND `|drive_start_timestamp - start_time|` <= window). On match: copies analytics fields into the Pi-sync row, redirects DriveStatistic/AnomalyLog drive_id pointers onto the survivor, deletes the analytics row. Idempotent. Reports merged + orphaned_analytics + orphaned_pi_sync counts.
- **Model docstring rewritten** (`src/server/db/models.py::DriveSummary`): removed the dual-writer + "two row families" prose; replaced with US-214 single-writer contract + invariants (one row per (source_device, drive_id), is_real=True only after analytics, Pi-sync owns metadata columns, table name permanent). No schema changes -- nullable columns preserved so the race path (analytics before Pi-sync) works + `_PRESERVE_ON_UPDATE` still protects source_device/source_id.
- **specs/architecture.md Section 5** updated (Drive-Start Metadata subsection): replaced "two writers co-exist" prose with "Reconciled single-writer semantics (US-214)" explaining the 4-step contract + race-safety + one-shot migration procedure.

Verify with `ssh mcornelison@10.27.27.10 'mysql obd2db -e "SELECT COUNT(*), COUNT(DISTINCT (source_device, drive_id)) FROM drive_summary WHERE source_device IS NOT NULL"'` -- post-reconciliation counts must match.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Find-or-create shape for dual-writer reconciliation**: when two writers co-exist on one table keyed differently, the most robust convergence is to make the one that runs later (analytics here) call a find-or-create that prefers the newer writer's natural key (source_device, drive_id). The older writer's legacy key stays as a fallback for pre-migration data. Race path (analytics runs before Pi-sync lands) is safe iff the later upsert path preserves the earlier writer's columns -- here via `_PRESERVE_ON_UPDATE` plus the fact that the Pi row doesn't carry those columns so they aren't in updateCols.
- **UNIQUE + NULL semantics is load-bearing**: `UNIQUE(source_device, source_id)` lets legacy analytics-only rows (source_device NULL) coexist without tripping the constraint because SQL standard treats NULL as distinct in UNIQUE. The reconciliation migration and the find-or-create both rely on this. If a future story ever tightens nullability to NOT NULL, it must also delete/reconcile legacy rows first.
- **is_real was never populated in production code pre-US-214**: grep showed it only set in tests. The calibration filter `is_real.is_(True)` was effectively filtering out all analytics-created rows until now. US-214 sets is_real=True in the reconciled update path -- calibration baselines should start seeing real drives again after the next auto-analysis run on a synced drive.
- **Scope manifest can have path drift**: US-214 scope.filesToTouch names `src/server/models/__init__.py` but actual server models live at `src/server/db/models.py`. Touched the correct path; documented in completionNotes so the PM sees the manifest drift on next sprint grooming.
- **DriveStatistic/AnomalyLog use integer drive_id without FK constraint**: deleting an analytics-only row during reconciliation would orphan any dependent stats. The migration issues UPDATE statements on those tables BEFORE the delete to redirect pointers. Future tables that reference `DriveSummary.id` need the same treatment.
