### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Detect at the boundary, don't re-architect the config shape**: The sprint contract allowed splitting `pi.bluetooth` into two keys (macAddress + serialPort). Chose instead to keep `macAddress` polymorphic — MAC or path — because the one-key shape is what every existing config.json / .env on the Pi already uses. The `isMacAddress()` check at connection-time costs nothing and preserves BC down to byte-level for any operator who had manually set `OBD_BT_MAC=/dev/rfcomm0` as the TD-023 workaround.

## 2026-04-19 - US-194 (Rex, Session 64)
Task: Fix TD-025 + TD-026 — SyncClient PK assumptions (id column + int cast)

### What was implemented:
- Hybrid **Option A (per-table PK registry)** + **Option B (split snapshot tables out)**.
- `sync_log.PK_COLUMN: dict[str, str]` — 6 append-only tables; `calibration_sessions` → `session_id`, others → `id`. Registry is authoritative; no runtime schema introspection.
- `sync_log.DELTA_SYNC_TABLES` — frozenset of append-only tables (6 members).
- `sync_log.SNAPSHOT_TABLES` — `{profiles, vehicle_info}`, explicitly excluded from delta-sync.
- `sync_log.IN_SCOPE_TABLES` preserved as the union (BC for server whitelist + `seed_pi_fixture.py` + integration fixtures).
- `sync_log._validateDeltaTable()` — narrower than `_validateTable`; rejects snapshot tables with `"not delta-syncable"` ValueError.
- `sync_log.getDeltaRows()` — uses `PK_COLUMN[tableName]` for cursor + `ORDER BY`; snapshot tables rejected cleanly.
- `SyncClient.PushStatus.SKIPPED` (new) — first-class deliberate-skip status.
- `SyncClient.pushDelta()` — snapshot tables short-circuit to SKIPPED before DB/network. High-water-mark advance reads `row[pkColumn]`.
- `SyncClient._renamePkToId(rows, pkColumn)` — renames `session_id` → `id` in payload rows so the existing server rule (`key == 'id'` → `source_id`) applies without server-side protocol change (honors stopCondition #1).
- `scripts/sync_now.py` dry-run — uses `PK_COLUMN`; snapshot tables render as `'delta-sync N/A'`.
- `specs/architecture.md` §Sync Log — added "US-194 (TD-025 + TD-026)" subsection.
- TD-025 + TD-026 both annotated **Closed** with closure notes referencing US-194.

### Files changed:

### Quality checks:
- Fast suite `pytest tests/ -m "not slow" -q` — 2336 passed / 8 skipped / 19 deselected / 0 failed in 439.14s (baseline 2295 + 41 new = 2336 exact; zero regressions).

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Hybrid Option A + Option B beats either pure approach when the PK variants aren't semantically uniform**: TD-025 framed the fix as either (A) per-table PK registry or (B) move upsert tables out of delta-sync. Three different PK shapes need different treatment: (1) `id INTEGER` standard five tables — no change beyond keeping them in delta-sync; (2) `session_id INTEGER` non-standard name, append-only semantics — needs the registry (Option A) to un-hardcode the column name; (3) `id TEXT` / `vin TEXT` snapshot tables — needs the split (Option B) because delta-by-PK is semantically meaningless for TEXT natural keys. Picking ONLY Option A forces `session_id` + `vin` + `'daily'` into the same code path with type-aware casting and lexicographic cursors (doable but semantically wrong). Picking ONLY Option B over-excludes `calibration_sessions` (an append-only table that genuinely delta-syncs once the PK name is known). Hybrid: registry for same-shape-different-name; split for different-shape-different-semantics. Pattern reusable for any "fix the assumption" refactor where the broken cases fall into distinct sub-categories.
- **Payload-level column rename (`session_id` → `id`) is cheaper than server-side rename rules — client owns the canonicalization**: the server's `_TABLE_REGISTRY` already has rename rules (e.g., `profiles: (("id", "source_profile_id"),)`) for Pi columns the server doesn't want literally. Adding `calibration_sessions: (("session_id", "id"),)` server-side would trigger the special-branch code path that assumes the renamed column is a synthetic integer — but `session_id` IS the authoritative PK. Cleaner: Pi renames `session_id` → `id` in each payload row via `_renamePkToId` before POSTing. Server sees an `id` key and maps via its DEFAULT rule (`key == 'id'` → `source_id`). Zero server-side changes. The rename must be TOTAL (new row, not a copy with both keys) because SQLAlchemy's `executemany` binds every key, and an unknown `session_id` would break the insert. Client keeps the source rows unchanged so the HWM advance still reads `max(row[pkColumn])` off the originals. Pattern reusable for any "local PK has non-canonical name" situation where both protocol sides are under your control but the protocol surface should stay small.
- **`PushStatus.SKIPPED` as a first-class deliberate-skip status**: the existing `PushStatus` enum had OK / FAILED / DISABLED / EMPTY. Snapshot tables don't fit any — not FAILED (no integrity issue), not DISABLED (service IS enabled), not EMPTY (table has rows, we just don't push them), not OK (nothing was pushed). Adding SKIPPED lets `pushAllDeltas()` still report one result per `IN_SCOPE_TABLES` (BC with operator output in `scripts/sync_now.py`) while distinguishing "deliberate no-op" from all others. Downstream consumers can ignore SKIPPED the same way they ignore EMPTY. Pattern reusable for any enum where "did nothing on purpose" is a distinct semantic from "did nothing because of a condition we already modeled".
- **Test harness stub schemas must mirror production PK shapes, not lowest-common-denominator**: US-149's `_createEmptyInScopeTables` helper gave every in-scope table an `id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT` — enough to satisfy `SELECT * WHERE id > ?` and make the push loop iterate without "no such table" errors. It passed for Sprint 11 and shipped. Session 23's real-drive push then crashed on `vehicle_info` (`vin TEXT PK`) + `calibration_sessions` (`session_id INTEGER PK`) — the test harness never saw it because every test table had `id`. Lesson: stub-table helpers for a whitelist that includes TEXT-PK or non-standard-name tables MUST mirror each table's production PK shape. Cost: ~10 extra lines in the helper, one branch on `tableName in SNAPSHOT_TABLES` or a registry lookup. Benefit: the same bug class can't ship twice. Applied at `tests/pi/sync/test_sync_client.py::_createEmptyInScopeTables` + `tests/integration/test_pi_to_server_e2e.py::_seededPiDb` (US-194). Reusable for any whitelist-iterated fixture helper.
---
- **Ownership tracking is the subtle half of idempotent lifecycle management**: Making `bindRfcomm` idempotent is easy. Making `disconnect()` safe to call whether the caller bound rfcomm themselves or inherited a pre-bound device is trickier. The `self._boundRfcomm` flag is set ONLY inside `_resolvePort` when a MAC was resolved, and is cleared inside `disconnect()` after (attempted) release. Path-passthrough operators who bound /dev/rfcomm0 via systemd never see `_boundRfcomm=True` and their lifecycle is preserved.
- **SubprocessRunner Protocol lets the same module run on Windows tests and Linux prod**: No `if sys.platform == 'linux'` guards. The default runner uses `subprocess.run` which on Windows just can't find `rfcomm` and raises `FileNotFoundError` -> `BluetoothHelperError`. Tests inject a `FakeRunner` that returns canned `CompletedProcess` objects. Same code path in both environments, zero platform-conditional imports.
- **Regex for a 6-octet-colon MAC is unambiguous against Linux device paths, Windows COM ports, and UUIDs**: `/dev/rfcomm0` lacks colons at the expected positions; `COM3` has no colons; UUID-format identifiers have different octet counts and separators. The single regex `^[0-9A-Fa-f]{2}(?::[0-9A-Fa-f]{2}){5}$` cleanly separates MAC from "anything else we should passthrough to pyserial".
- **Bash helper vs sudoers NOPASSWD is a deployment choice, not a design choice**: Both are documented in `specs/architecture.md` §3.4. The Python helper doesn't care which one the operator picks. The sudoers entry is cleaner (narrower scope: only `/usr/sbin/rfcomm`, not a generic sudo-grant); the bash helper is more portable to environments where sudoers can't be edited. Both are live.
---

MAC from argv or `$OBD_BT_MAC`. `--dry-run` is a true preview (no BT stack invocation). Pre-flight checks bluetoothctl + python3 pexpect availability.

- `specs/architecture.md` §3.4 — expanded: SSP passkey flow + bt-agent gotcha, pair-mode re-trigger UX (30s + solid blue LED), bond vs rfcomm-bind persistence distinction, two-layer reboot-survival (systemd unit + self-heal on `connect()`), new env-file config table, ISO 9141-2 empirical confirmation.
- `docs/testing.md` — new OBDLink LX Bluetooth Walkthrough section with 5 procedures (A pair, B daily rfcomm bind, C install reboot-survival, D simulate-reboot verification, E troubleshooting table).

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered**: Bash wrapper + embedded python3 heredoc keeps shellcheck-clean arg parsing on the bash side AND keeps pexpect in a single file (no sibling `.py`). Export variables to the heredoc via `export MAC` instead of shell-interpolating into the python block.
- **Pattern discovered**: `PATH` shim with a fake binary that writes a sentinel file is the cleanest way to prove `--dry-run` really doesn't invoke an external tool. Prepend a tempdir with a fake `bluetoothctl` that `echo called > sentinel; exit 0`, run the script, then assert the sentinel doesn't exist.
- **Pattern discovered**: systemd `Type=oneshot + RemainAfterExit=yes` is the right shape for "binding is state, not a running process" work like `rfcomm bind`. `systemctl is-active` returns `active` even though no process is still running.
- **Gotcha**: `deploy-pi.sh --init` step ordering matters — rfcomm-bind install MUST run AFTER `sync_tree` because the installer script itself is synced from Windows.
- **Gotcha**: Test the "no hardcoded MAC" invariant in BOTH the script body AND heredoc content. Example strings in `--help` that quote a full MAC will trip a naive grep-for-comments-only test — use a placeholder like `AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:FF` in docs.
- **Gotcha**: `EnvironmentFile=/etc/default/obdlink` in the unit needs `ConditionPathExists=/etc/default/obdlink` pair to avoid a startup failure when the operator hasn't run the installer yet.

## 2026-04-19 - US-198
Task: Fix TD-024 status_display GL BadAccess under X11

### What was implemented:
- New StatusDisplay constructor arg `forceSoftwareRenderer` (default True).
- Before `pygame.init()`, inject SDL env hints (`SDL_RENDER_DRIVER=software`, `SDL_VIDEO_X11_FORCE_EGL=0`, `SDL_FRAMEBUFFER_ACCELERATION=0`) only if the operator hasn't already set them in the environment (`.service` files win).
- New `forceSoftwareRenderer` read-only property on StatusDisplay.
- Threaded `displayForceSoftwareRenderer` through `HardwareManager.__init__` and `createHardwareManagerFromConfig`.
- New config keys `pi.hardware.statusDisplay.{enabled, forceSoftwareRenderer}` (both default true). `statusDisplay.enabled` takes precedence over legacy `display.enabled` for the overlay.
- TD-024 annotated Closed with fix summary + rejected-options rationale.
- specs/architecture.md §10 Display Architecture: new "Two Display Surfaces" subsection documenting the primary / overlay split and the TD-024 rationale.

### Files changed:
- Modified: `src/pi/hardware/status_display.py` (forceSoftwareRenderer arg, SDL env hints helper `_applySoftwareRendererHints`, property, header entry)
- Modified: `src/pi/hardware/hardware_manager.py` (displayForceSoftwareRenderer constructor arg, factory wiring, statusDisplay config keys, header entry)
- Modified: `config.json` (new `pi.hardware.statusDisplay` block)
- Modified: `specs/architecture.md` (Two Display Surfaces subsection under §10)
- Modified: `offices/pm/tech_debt/TD-024-status-display-gl-badaccess-x11.md` (Closed + fix summary)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/sprint.json` (US-198 passes:true + completionNotes)
- Created: `tests/pi/hardware/test_status_display.py` (11 tests across 5 classes)
- Created: `tests/pi/hardware/test_manager_status_display_disable.py` (7 tests across 3 classes)

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered**: For SDL2/pygame GL issues under X11, env hints MUST be set before `pygame.init()` — the video subsystem reads them exactly once at startup. Use `os.environ.setdefault`-style logic (only fill if unset) so operator `.service` overrides win.
- **Pattern discovered**: Xlib's `XIOError` handler calls `exit()` on `BadAccess`, so Python `try/except` cannot catch it. The fix MUST prevent the GL context request from happening, not catch it after. This is why Option (b) (try/except fallback) was rejected in US-198 even though it sounds obvious.
- **Gotcha**: Tests that exercise `_refreshLoop` need to trip `_stopEvent` from WITHIN the side_effect (not before calling the loop) — the loop's `while not self._stopEvent.is_set()` short-circuits before the body runs if the event is pre-set, so the test validates nothing.
- **Gotcha**: `pi.display.manager`'s Headless/Minimal/Developer drivers do NOT call `pygame.display.set_mode` — the primary driving screen surface is only created by `scripts/render_primary_screen_live.py` (out-of-process). So the overlay vs primary conflict is NOT the root cause of TD-024; it was genuinely the overlay's own GL context request under X11.
- **Gotcha**: When mocking pygame for tests, `sys.modules["pygame"]` only catches top-level `import pygame` — the status_display code does `import pygame` inside functions, which Python resolves via sys.modules at call time, so the monkeypatch works. But you ALSO need to pre-register `pygame.font`, `pygame.display`, etc. as ModuleType objects because pygame submodule access (`pygame.font.SysFont`) evaluates attribute lookup on the top-level module first — the fake module must carry those submodules as attributes too (the fixture `pygameInModuleRegistry` handles both).

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered (agent.md refactor)**: Slim core (≤400 lines with topic→file mapping table) + load-on-demand knowledge subsidiaries (≤400 each) + explicit load-decision rules in knowledge/README.md. Canonical approach for Ralph-owned knowledge now. Core carries always-needed content (CIO Dev Rules, Golden Code Patterns, Git/PM protocol, workflow); subsidiaries carry topic-gated patterns.
- **Pattern discovered (cross-doc duplication handling)**: specs/ is PM-owned (per agent.md "specs is read-only for Ralph" rule). Ralph cannot refactor PM-owned duplication directly. File an issue (I-017 precedent) and let Marcus groom a canonicalization story. Session 71's Q2 answer from CIO was (c) mixed: Ralph-owned now, specs via PM-requested stories in Sprint 16+.
- **Gotcha (knowledge-log vs actual-fix gap)**: logging a drift observation in session-learnings.md without a corresponding TD does NOT result in a fix. The ralph.sh passes/passed typo sat in session-learnings.md for unknown sessions before CIO saw the visible contradiction and asked for a review. New CIO Q1 rule (2026-04-20): file TD immediately on observing drift outside sprint; fix inline only if current-scope permission applies.
- **Gotcha (session-handoff rot)**: session-handoff.md can silently drift multiple sessions. At /init-ralph when handoff disagrees with ralph_agents.json per-agent note, TRUST the per-agent note — it's written every close. Cross-check handoff vs agent-state vs git log vs recent inbox notes before trusting any one source.
- **Gotcha (shell grep against JSON schema)**: `grep -c '"field": true' file.json 2>/dev/null || echo 0` silently returns 0 on a field-name typo. If a counter reads a schema, it needs an assertion path or a `python -c 'import json'` lookup — not a `|| echo 0` fallback that hides broken matches. This was already in session-learnings.md but unfixed until Session 71; entry retained.
- **Pattern discovered (Tier 3 code observations)**: Low-urgency flags from reading Sprint 14 modules — (1) drive_id.py::nextDriveId has multi-connection race comment; (2) engine_state.py::_handleRunning defaults missing speed to 0.0 (conservative for 2G SPEED gaps); (3) main.py dual sys.path setup supports both `from common.*` and `from src.common.*`; (4) server/main.py lifespan warns-but-continues on DB init failure — downstream endpoints need null-engine guards; (5) orchestrator/core.py::runLoop is supervisor, not poll loop. All flagged in Sprint 15 review note for reviewer awareness; none filed as TDs (not urgent enough).
- **Pattern discovered (I-016 thermostat attach-to-story)**: investigation-gated issues don't need their own story. Attach a drill-protocol addendum to a story already scheduled to collect the needed data (US-208 first-drive in Sprint 15). Saves a story slot; resolves the hanging auto-memory item; matches "if data confirms X close benign, else promote to hardware story" branching logic.

### Files changed:

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered (defensive Python SSH orchestrator)**: CommandRunner Protocol as injectable seam lets you test SSH-dependent scripts without mocking subprocess at the module level. FakeRunner pattern with needle-matching on argv or stdin payload covers 22 tests comprehensively. Use `Path.as_posix()` when passing paths to `bash -c` on Windows -- backslashes and UNC paths break bash resolution; forward slashes work on both MSYS2 and POSIX.
- **Gotcha (DEFAULT 'real' collects everything post-migration)**: US-195's `DEFAULT 'real'` on data_source made "tagged real" equivalent to "written after US-195 shipped" rather than "captured from real vehicle." Any operator using `WHERE data_source='real'` needs to validate whether tagged-real matches vehicle-real; the gap is subtle and easy to miss at story-spec time.
- **Gotcha (SQLAlchemy model changes != live-DB migration)**: US-195/200 Pi code adds `drive_id INTEGER` etc. to the SQLite tables via `ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN` at boot (ObdDatabase.initialize). Server-side analogues only shipped in SQLAlchemy model definitions; there's no runtime migration hook on the server. Ship schema catchup as a deliberate story -- never assume model-dict-changes propagate.
- **Gotcha (SQLite locked under running service)**: Any script that opens data/obd.db while eclipse-obd.service is active hits "database is locked (5)". Use SSH to stop the service before operations, even read operations, because readers can race with long-held write transactions. Script auto-handles stop/start for --execute; operator must know for manual dry-run invocations.
- **Pattern discovered (dry-run sentinel gate)**: writing a sentinel file after successful dry-run and requiring it to exist before --execute creates an explicit handshake that can't be bypassed with argv parsing tricks. Deleting the sentinel on execute-success forces re-dry-run on next iteration.
- **Pattern discovered (schema-aware DELETE refusal)**: when a schema divergence is detected, returning a reason-list that the operator sees verbatim beats returning a single boolean. Multi-reason divergence (9 reasons here) tells the operator exactly which migrations need to run; single-bool would obscure the fact that server-side US-195 AND US-200 are both missing.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered (sys.meta_path finder + importlib.reload to force ImportError deterministically)**: testing module-level import-catching code on a system where the real imports succeed requires a way to force the failure path. Registering an `_ExplodingFinder` on `sys.meta_path` that raises `ImportError` for specific module prefixes + popping the target module from `sys.modules` + `importlib.import_module(...)` re-executes the try/except under synthetic failure conditions. Clean up in a `try/finally` (remove finder, restore blocked modules, reimport the real module). Used for TD-015 `test_hardwareImportError_emitsInfoLog_whenImportFails`.
- **Pattern discovered (subprocess-CLI-test -> main(args)-call conversion)**: CLI tests that exercise an entry-point function like `main(args) -> int` should call `main([args])` in-process instead of `subprocess.run([sys.executable, script.py, ...])` whenever possible. The contract under test is the exit-code return value -- same with or without the subprocess boundary. The subprocess adds ~50-200s Windows Store Python cold-start latency per call + introduces a timeout knob that becomes a flake vector. In-process calls are milliseconds and deterministic. Only use subprocess when testing the actual process-boundary behavior (signals, env isolation, argv parsing via `sys.argv` mutation).
- **Pattern discovered (call-count-driven test shutdown)**: wall-clock `time.sleep(N)` in a shutdown-triggering thread creates a flake window -- under load, the main loop may not complete enough iterations before the sleep fires. Instead, drive shutdown from inside the instrumented callback when a known call-count threshold is reached. Trade-off: makes the test white-box on the callback call pattern, but the alternative is non-deterministic.
- **Gotcha (`# noqa` on probe imports)**: `scripts/check_platform.py` imports libraries that may not be installed to check availability (`import dotenv` etc.). `ruff` flags these as F401 and suggests `importlib.util.find_spec`. But `find_spec` ONLY checks module discoverability -- it doesn't execute init-time side-effects. A package like `board` (adafruit-blinka) has init-time platform checks that raise `NotImplementedError` on non-Pi systems; the try/ImportError pattern detects this, `find_spec` doesn't. Use `# noqa: F401 -- probe import` instead of rewriting.
- **Gotcha (`ruff --fix` splits `from X import (A, B, C as D)` when `D` is the only aliased name)**: when running `ruff --fix` on `from scripts.verify_database import (initializeAndVerify, main as verifyDatabaseCliMain, verifyDatabase)`, ruff re-ordered the imports alphabetically AND split them across two `from scripts.verify_database import ...` statements -- one for the plain names, one for the aliased name. Not a bug, just surprising. Resulting code is still clean.

Also flags the SQLAlchemy `Integer` → `BigInteger` fix for drive_id columns.

### Files changed:
- Created: `scripts/apply_server_migrations.py` (~580 LOC, stdlib-only, SSH-orchestrated)
- Created: `tests/scripts/test_apply_server_migrations.py` (39 tests)
- Created: `offices/pm/tech_debt/TD-029-server-migrations-not-auto-applied.md`
- Modified: `specs/architecture.md` (§5 Drive Lifecycle Invariant #4 + new US-209 catch-up paragraph)
- Modified: `docs/testing.md` (new Server Schema Migration Runbook section)

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Gotcha (default-arg capture of module-level `_defaultRunner`)**: Python binds function defaults at definition time. When `def foo(runner=_defaultRunner)` is defined, the NAME `_defaultRunner` resolves once; later `monkeypatch.setattr(asm, '_defaultRunner', fake)` replaces the module attribute but does NOT affect functions whose defaults are already bound. Fix: either `runner=None` + inside-function resolution `runner = runner or _defaultRunner`, OR explicit pass-through from `main()` (the approach I took). This pattern affects every CLI-level test that needs to inject a runner via a module global. Rex's truncate_session23.py happens to avoid this because the tests pass `runner=FakeRunner` explicitly rather than relying on default resolution.
- **Gotcha (class-level monkey-patching in FakeRunner tests)**: a test that writes `runner.__class__.__call__ = lambda ...` (intending to swap per-instance) actually modifies the CLASS, not the instance. Dataclass instances share the class `__call__` slot. So the change persists across tests, corrupting subsequent ones. The truncate test file has this pattern in `TestScanPiState`; it worked only because that was the last scan test executed. My `TestScanServerSchema` hit the same pattern and produced cascading `assert 0 == 2` failures until I replaced the class-level patch with a plain function satisfying the CommandRunner Protocol. Plain functions are always preferable to dataclass instances for Protocol conformance -- no persistent mutation surface.
- **Pattern (MariaDB DDL can't be transactionally rolled back)**: ALTER TABLE and CREATE TABLE are implicit-commit operations in MariaDB. Wrapping them in `START TRANSACTION` / `COMMIT` is legal syntax but provides no rollback semantics -- the DDL commits immediately. The correct safety net is `mysqldump --single-transaction` BEFORE any DDL; on failure the operator restores via `mysql < backup.sql`. My script makes this explicit in both the docstring and the rollback procedure in docs/testing.md.
- **Pattern (constants-parity tests prevent schema drift)**: TestConstantsParity imports `src.pi.obdii.data_source.CAPTURE_TABLES` + `src.pi.obdii.drive_id.DRIVE_ID_TABLES` + `DRIVE_COUNTER_TABLE` at test time and asserts set-equality with the server-script constants. If a future Pi-side story adds a capture table without updating US-209's scope, the server script silently omits that table from migrations -- the test catches this drift loudly. Analogous to Session 73's `test_ralph_promise_tag_contract.py` but for schema scope.
- **Pattern (DDL ordering matters for idempotency probes)**: `planMigrations` must emit data_source columns first, drive_id columns second, drive_id indexes third, drive_counter table last. A freshly-added drive_id column will have `hasDriveIdIndex=False` at scan time because the probe ran before the ALTER; so the plan unconditionally requests the index when *either* column or index is missing. Re-running on a fully-migrated DB correctly emits zero statements because the probe sees both present.

- Modified: `offices/ralph/ralph_agents.json` (Agent 3 status + note)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/progress.txt` (this entry)

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern (preserve operator state across destructive SSH scripts)**: the try/finally idiom `finally: startService()` over-eagerly restores state the operator didn't ask for. Capture `priorServiceActive = service.is_active()` BEFORE stopping, and only restart in the finally block if it was active at entry. Applies to any script that stops a service to hold a lock: truncate, schema migrate, large-batch import, etc. Otherwise the operator's deliberate "keep it stopped" state is violated one SSH round-trip after the script completes.
- **Gotcha (SQLite probe returns silent 0 under write lock)**: when chi-eclipse-01's eclipse-obd.service is actively writing, `sqlite3 .../obd.db "PRAGMA table_info(...)"` errors out with "database is locked (5)" and `_parseColumnsSqlite` returns `[]`, which the script interpreted as "column absent" and produced spurious divergence reasons. The pre-dry-run step should be: stop the Pi service, wait for lock release, then probe. I added this as a manual operator step rather than coding it into the script -- ambiguous automation given the script already stops the service inside --execute. If a future run trips over this, the right fix is `probePiColumns` raising on non-zero returncode instead of silently returning `[]`, so the operator gets a loud "probe failed -- service holding lock?" message instead of a quiet misclassification.
- **Pattern (running --execute twice is the realistic idempotency story)**: the first --execute succeeded but the finally block's force-restart repopulated 5 rows before the next SSH stop; I re-ran --execute with the service pre-stopped and got a truly clean state. The script's DELETE + UPDATE are idempotent by design (0 rows to delete + drive_counter already 0 = no-op), so the double-run has no ill effect. Tests now pin this behavior (priorActive=False -> no restart).
- **Pattern (Spool-amendment-compliant alert_log handling)**: Pi-side data_source.py::CAPTURE_TABLES intentionally excludes alert_log (no sim/replay/fixture writes target it). US-209 honored the same shape on the server side. divergenceDetected's carve-out must mirror on both loops, otherwise --execute refuses over a deliberate schema difference. Script's DELETE path already skipped alert_log via hasDataSourceColumn=False check; the carve-out is purely on the divergence-refusal side.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern (registry-as-source-of-truth for sync table sets)**: adding `'dtc_log': 'id'` to `PK_COLUMN` in `src/pi/data/sync_log.py` automatically propagates to `DELTA_SYNC_TABLES` (a frozenset(PK_COLUMN.keys())) and `IN_SCOPE_TABLES` (DELTA | SNAPSHOT). One-line change to add a delta-syncable table. Server side still needs an explicit `_TABLE_REGISTRY` entry though -- two surfaces to remember.
- **Pattern (parity-test maintenance when adding a synced table)**: adding a delta-sync table breaks 4 categories of existing tests: (a) hardcoded count assertions (DELTA_SYNC_TABLES len, ACCEPTED_TABLES set, total table count), (b) IN_SCOPE_TABLES iterators that build per-table fixture stubs (test_sync_client_upsert, test_pi_to_server_e2e, test_seed_pi_fixture), (c) seed fixture INSERTs, (d) the new sync test itself. Categories (a) and (b) are mandatory; (c) is mandatory only if the seed script reads IN_SCOPE_TABLES dynamically (it does for sync_log seeding but not for per-table inserts). Plan to touch all 4 categories on the next addition.
- **Pattern (MIL rising-edge as a tiny class, not a free function)**: stateful detection works cleanest as a class because `_handleReading` doesn't have a natural place to stash "previous value" -- adding it as an instance attribute on the orchestrator would couple it to one hot-path branch. Standalone class with `observe()` returning bool keeps the dispatch site one line and the state contained. The `reset()` hook lets `_handleDriveStart` re-baseline so a freshly-illuminated MIL on a new drive's first poll correctly fires the re-fetch.
- **Pattern (orchestrator-side dispatch swallows exceptions)**: `_dispatchSessionStartDtcs` and `_dispatchMilEventDtcs` both wrap their `dtcLogger` call in try/except + logger.warning. Drive-start and reading-handle paths must never crash -- the orchestrator's poll loop is the heartbeat; an OBD adapter glitch during DTC fetch must NOT propagate. Tests pin this behavior explicitly (`test_swallowsExceptions`, `test_swallowsMilDispatchFailure`).
- **Pattern (probe-first for 2G optional commands)**: `Mode07ProbeResult` returned from `readPendingDtcs` lets the caller cache "unsupported" per-connection without persisting it. Reconnect re-probes (cheap; survives hardware swaps). Same shape would work for any future "may or may not be supported" optional Mode -- reuse the dataclass for Mode 09 InfoType queries when those land.
- **Pattern (off-Pi command factory injection seam)**: `commandFactory: Callable[[str], Any]` parameter on DtcClient makes tests pass with string command names while production wires through `defaultCommandFactory` which lazy-imports `obd.commands.<name>`. Same pattern would work for any python-obd-dependent class on Windows dev (ObdConnection, queryParameter etc. don't yet do this -- they degrade via the missing-module path). Worth proposing for future hardening of Pi-only modules.
- **Gotcha (ruff catches unused imports after refactor)**: when I added the imports to test files I included some unused names (DiagnosticCode in test_dtc_logger after the refactor moved that assertion to a different test, pytest in test_dtc_dispatch when I switched to a class-based exception path). `ruff check --fix` cleanly removed them. Keep `ruff --fix` in the standard test-file completion ritual.

- Created: `offices/pm/inbox/2026-04-20-from-ralph-us206-drive-summary-reconciliation-note.md`

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered (Additive column extension for dual-writer tables)**: when Spool / PM specify a table name that already exists server-side for a different writer path, the cleanest path is to ADD nullable columns + a second UNIQUE constraint rather than rename or split. The two writers coexist because SQL-standard UNIQUE treats NULLs as distinct — analytics writer leaves Pi-sync cols NULL, Pi-sync writer leaves analytics cols NULL. Requires widening formerly-NOT-NULL cols (device_id, start_time, is_real on DriveSummary) to nullable. Trade-off: two row families per drive until a reconciliation story merges them — noted in inbox.
- **Pattern discovered (Lightweight state tracking for cold-start rule without full state machine)**: the DriveDetector's RPM-threshold-driven lifecycle is parallel to US-200's EngineStateMachine. Rather than wire the full machine in, a `_lastEngineState: EngineState` attribute with UNKNOWN default + KEY_OFF set in _endDrive + RUNNING set after _startDrive gives the cold-start rule the fromState it needs with no refactoring risk. The story's Spool acceptance referenced `engine_state.lastTransition.fromState` — this attribute satisfies the semantics without importing the full classifier.
- **Gotcha (read-only snapshot consumers must not trigger ECU polls)**: US-206 Invariant #1 required `getLatestReadings()` to NOT trigger new polls. Added the cache update at the TAIL of `queryParameter` (after the reading is produced) and `_queryViaDecoder` (same spot). This keeps the "only-populated-from-actual-polls" contract strict — a caller reading the snapshot between polls sees the last-successful value per param; an empty dict if no polls have completed yet (cold start between boot and first tick).
- **Gotcha (ObdDatabase.connect wraps IntegrityError)**: test that asserts CHECK constraint rejection needs to `pytest.raises((sqlite3.IntegrityError, DatabaseConnectionError))` — ObdDatabase.connect re-raises wrapped. Learned this when `test_dataSourceCheckConstraintRejectsBogus` failed on first pass; same gotcha likely applies to other schema-constraint tests.
- **Gotcha (naming collision with existing DriveSummary)**: the spec path `src/server/models/__init__.py` didn't exist (actual is `src/server/db/models.py`) and the existing server `DriveSummary` class is used by 8+ files across analytics/reports. Discovered this via grep BEFORE writing server-side code. Filed a detailed reconciliation note + chose the additive-extension path to avoid touching analytics code. Lesson: always grep for the exact class name across `src/server/` before designing a new model that uses the same name.

- Modified: `specs/architecture.md` (Section 5 Drive Lifecycle -- End-to-end verification paragraph)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/sprint.json` (US-208 passes:true + feedback block)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/ralph_agents.json` (close note; status unassigned)

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered (validator with --fixture-db for off-Pi testability)**: Bash validators that rely on SSH + remote sqlite3 CLI are hard to unit-test on dev machines. A single `sqlite_query_pi()` helper that conditionally routes through either `ssh+sqlite3` (live mode) OR `sqlite3 $FIXTURE_DB` (off-Pi mode) makes the same queries work in both contexts. Tests build a synthetic fixture in tmp_path and run the real bash script against it. Mirrors `verify_live_idle.sh --bench`.
- **Pattern discovered (Python-native mirror of bash queries for cross-platform tests)**: When sqlite3 CLI is a test prereq that Windows dev machines lack, mirror the bash SQL strings in a Python `_SQL_*` constants block and test them via `sqlite3.connect().execute()`. Doesn't replace the bash-invocation tests (they still run on Pi/CI), but keeps acceptance coverage green on all dev platforms. The two copies must be kept in sync; the structural test `test_driverContainsRequiredFlags` can be paired with a future `test_validator_sql_strings_still_match_python_mirrors` check (not added here since the SQL is simple; add it only if complexity grows).
- **Gotcha (awk float-compare + julianday duration)**: Bash arithmetic is integer-only. For "is 85.3 >= 82.0" use `awk -v m="$max" -v t="$thresh" 'BEGIN{print (m+0 >= t+0) ? 1 : 0}'`. For drive-duration minutes from ISO-8601 timestamps, let sqlite do it: `CAST((julianday(MAX(timestamp)) - julianday(MIN(timestamp))) * 1440 AS INTEGER)`. The `* 1440` converts Julian day fraction to minutes.
- **Gotcha (B-044 catches dry-run help text)**: The audit lint flags hardcoded hostnames even inside help/heredoc strings. Fix via `$SERVER_HOSTNAME` / `$PI_HOSTNAME` substitution rather than a `# b044-exempt:` pragma — the canonical bash address mirror already exports them, so the substitution keeps the docs self-consistent for free.
- **Gotcha (activity-gated acceptance)**: When a story requires a hardware event (real drive) that may not happen in the sprint window, the story MUST include an explicit fallback path (off-Pi test + dry-run green = acceptance). Validator output must distinguish N/A ("drive didn't happen") from FAIL ("drive happened but data wrong") — the summary count `$PASS_COUNT / $FAIL_COUNT / $NA_COUNT` is the right shape for this.

- 13 US-210 targeted tests PASS

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered**: systemd drop-ins beat editing vendor files. Drop-in at
  /etc/systemd/journald.conf.d/99-*.conf survives apt upgrades and gives clear
  provenance -- every setting in conf.d/ is ours. Idempotent install via
  `cmp -s source target` pattern: only restart the unit when the file actually
  changed. Applied this here; reusable for any future systemd config tweak.
- **Pattern discovered**: flipping an existing test assertion is a red-flag
  diff. The BL-004 regression guard at test_eclipse_obd_service.py:46-55 had
  been there since Sprint 11 asserting --simulate IS present. US-210 was the
  planned sunset for that assertion, but a future reviewer needs a breadcrumb
  so they don't think the test was sabotaged. Resolution: keep the function
  name similar but invert (execStartPassesSimulateFlag -> execStartOmitsSimulateFlag)
  and write the docstring as "US-210 FLIPPED the BL-004 carveout". Git blame
  + test docstring = audit trail.
- **Gotcha**: src/pi/main.py banner must print BEFORE setupLogging() runs. If
  it prints after, the logger handlers may swallow/reformat it and the
  sentinel literal no longer appears verbatim in journalctl. Tests/pi asserts
  on capsys stdout to lock this ordering.
- **Gotcha**: /var/log/journal creation is systemd-journald responsibility
  when Storage=persistent is set, but the directory only appears after
  `systemctl restart systemd-journald`. Our install step reloads (via
  restart) only when the drop-in content changed, and post-checks the
  directory via `[ ! -d /var/log/journal ] && exit 7`. Without the
  post-check, a permissions hiccup would silently drop logs.
- **Gotcha**: shellcheck absent on Windows git-bash. Acceptance criterion
  "where shellcheck is available on the runner" covers this, but future
  Ralph sessions on Linux should rerun shellcheck on modified .sh files
  (here: deploy/deploy-pi.sh).

## 2026-04-21 - US-211 - BT-Resilient Collector

### What was implemented:
- Four new Python modules driving the BT-resilience layer:
  * `src/pi/data/connection_logger.py` -- canonical event_type constants
    (EVENT_BT_DISCONNECT, EVENT_ADAPTER_WAIT, EVENT_RECONNECT_ATTEMPT,
    EVENT_RECONNECT_SUCCESS, EVENT_ECU_SILENT_WAIT) + logConnectionEvent
    helper. Swallows DB exceptions so observability never crashes capture.
  * `src/pi/obdii/error_classification.py` -- pure classifyCaptureError()
    returning CaptureErrorClass enum (ADAPTER_UNREACHABLE / ECU_SILENT /
    FATAL). Lazy imports + substring matching against rfcomm/bluez stderr
    shapes keep the classifier self-contained.
  * `src/pi/obdii/reconnect_loop.py` -- ReconnectLoop class with
    DEFAULT_BACKOFF_SCHEDULE=(1,5,10,30,60) + BACKOFF_CAP_SECONDS=60.
    Injectable probe/eventLogger/sleepFn/shouldExitFn for deterministic
    tests. reset() rewinds on success. buildDefaultReconnectLoop() factory.
  * `src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/bt_resilience.py` -- BtResilienceMixin
    exposes handleCaptureError(exc) -> CaptureErrorClass. ADAPTER tears
    down + runs loop + reopens; ECU_SILENT stays connected; FATAL
    re-raises to systemd.
- Extended `src/pi/obdii/bluetooth_helper.py` with isRfcommReachable()
  two-layer probe (stat /dev/rfcommN + rfcomm show). Swallows all
  exceptions -> False so the reconnect loop never crashes.

  orchestrator/core.py. _reconnectLoopFactory init; production falls
  through to _defaultLoopFactory using live DB + MAC + rfcommDevice.
- connection_log.event_type stays TEXT (no CHECK) -- ADDITIVE invariant
  takes precedence; existing dynamic writers (profile switcher
  event.eventType, shutdown f'shutdown_{event}') would break under a
  restrictive CHECK. Canonical set is Python-level in
  connection_logger.py + documented in schema comment.
- specs/architecture.md: new Collector Resilience subsection with error
  taxonomy table, reconnect loop behavior, connection_log timeline,
  5 invariants.

  6-step procedure + off-Pi test path + systemd-restart sanity.

### Quality gates (Windows runner):

- Ruff: clean on all 12 touched files
- validate_config: 4/4 OK
- sprint_lint: 0 errors (informational sizing warnings pre-existing)

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern -- classifier ordering with subclass inheritance**: Python
  3.10+ makes TimeoutError a subclass of OSError. A classifier that
  checks `isinstance(exc, OSError)` FIRST catches every TimeoutError
  and false-classifies BT-free timeouts as ADAPTER_UNREACHABLE. Fix:
  check TimeoutError/ObdConnectionTimeoutError BEFORE the generic
  OSError branch. Pin with a dedicated boundary test
  (test_classifyCaptureError_timeoutWithRfcommSignature_isAdapter) so
  refactoring doesn't regress.
- **Pattern -- Python-level enum vs SQL CHECK for free-text columns**:
  When a column has dynamic writers emitting runtime-composed strings
  (f'shutdown_{event}', event.eventType from event objects), a
  restrictive SQL CHECK constraint would break them. Solution: keep
  the column free-text + document canonical set in a Python module +
  add a grep-style audit test that walks src/pi/ and asserts every
  canonical literal is referenced somewhere. Satisfies "additive +
  accepts new values" cleanly.
- **Pattern -- injection-based async state-machine testing**: Instead
  of threading + time.sleep + os.path.exists + rfcomm calls, pass
  (probe, eventLogger, sleepFn, shouldExitFn) via constructor
  injection. FakeProbe iterates scripted bool results, FakeSleep
  collects durations, FakeEventLogger collects events. Tests run in
  ~0 wall-clock and assert exact sequences at both unit + integration
  level.
- **Pattern -- mixin composition for orthogonal orchestrator capabilities**:
  Existing ConnectionRecoveryMixin handles state-change-driven
  reconnection via background thread. US-211 needed synchronous
  error-class-driven reconnection. Added parallel BtResilienceMixin
  rather than rewriting. Both compose into ApplicationOrchestrator;
  callers pick the path that fits. Legacy path can be narrowed over
  time without a flag day.
- **Gotcha**: TimeoutError is OSError subclass (Python 3.10+).
  `issubclass(TimeoutError, OSError)` returns True. Order classifier
  branches accordingly.
- **Gotcha**: connection_log.event_type column has NO CHECK constraint
  even though adjacent capture tables have CHECK on data_source.
  Dynamic writers rely on this freedom -- don't add a CHECK.
- **Gotcha**: Windows dev runners have no /dev/rfcomm0, so the default
  os.path.exists always returns False. Tests inject pathExists=
  lambda _: True to simulate the Pi side. Keep the probe injectable.
- **Gotcha**: orchestrator/__init__.py re-exports ApplicationOrchestrator
  from core.py. Adding a new mixin only touches core.py; __init__.py
  re-export stays unchanged. Public surface stays narrow.

### Quality gates (Windows runner):
- Fast suite: **2943 passed** (+44 new vs 2899 US-212 baseline, 0
  regressions, 17 skipped, 19 deselected, 551.09s)
- New tests: 44/44 green (36 server + 8 deploy)
- US-209 tests: 39/39 green (unchanged)
- Ruff check src/server/migrations/ scripts/apply_server_migrations.py
  tests/server/test_migrations.py tests/deploy/test_deploy_server_
  migration_gate.py: all clean
- validate_config.py: 4/4 OK
- sprint_lint.py: 0 errors (3 pre-existing informational sizing warnings
  on US-213 unchanged)

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern -- explicit migration registry**: For hand-rolled schema
  migration without Alembic, use a `Migration` dataclass (version,
  description, applyFn) + an ordered `ALL_MIGRATIONS` tuple + a runner
  that bookkeeps in a `schema_migrations` table (version PK, description,
  applied_at default CURRENT_TIMESTAMP). Runner: ensureTracking (CREATE
  IF NOT EXISTS) + getApplied (SELECT version) + planPending (filter) +
  apply + _recordApplied (INSERT after successful applyFn so partial
  success is observable). Matches Pi-side ensure* idempotent patterns.
- **Pattern -- retroactive registration of a one-shot migration**: When
  closing a deploy-flow bug that was previously patched manually via a
  one-shot script, register that script's DDL as migration 0001 so the
  bookkeeping table shows the full history on servers that already
  manually applied it. Migration's applyFn is idempotent (empty plan on
  already-migrated DB), so the first post-gate deploy records '0001'
  with no DDL emitted.
- **Pattern -- function-local cross-boundary import**: When the new
  migration registry imports symbols from scripts/apply_server_migrations
  AND apply_server_migrations's new --run-all mode needs to import from
  the registry, break the obvious cycle by doing a function-local import
  inside apply_server_migrations's runRegistry() helper. Registry-side
  top-level imports stay; apply_server_migrations module load no longer
  drags in the registry. Registry side pulls in apply_server_migrations
  at load time, which is fine because apply_server_migrations has no
  static top-level dependency on the registry.
- **Pattern -- 'enhance don't replace' invariant**: When scope says
  enhance an existing script, add new CLI mode(s) alongside legacy modes
  rather than rewriting the legacy path. Run both sets of tests
  together; any regression on the legacy path surfaces immediately.
  US-213 kept 39 US-209 tests green + added 44 new tests, total 83
  across the migration surface.
- **Pattern -- deploy-script static invariants as tests**: Instead of
  trying to run deploy-server.sh in CI (needs SSH, live MariaDB), assert
  invariants via text-content checks: `set -e` present, --run-all called,
  the call line is NOT nested under an `if INIT=true` only block, call
  position precedes service-start, call position follows pip install.
  Catches deploy-time structural regressions at PR time.
- **Gotcha -- str.find in deploy-script tests**: Adding documentation
  strings to the header comment (e.g., mentioning `--run-all`) can skew
  str.find positions. Fix: anchor test searches to the executable body
  (after the `set -e` marker) so header comments don't interfere.
- **Gotcha -- importlib vs package import**: scripts/ has __init__.py so
  `from scripts import apply_server_migrations` works (clean path). The
  existing tests/scripts/test_apply_server_migrations.py uses importlib
  for historical reasons; new callers can skip that workaround.
- **Gotcha -- schema_migrations tracking row order**: Insert the row
  AFTER the applyFn succeeds, never before. Inserting before means a
  mid-plan failure leaves a ghost row that suppresses future re-runs;
  inserting after means partial success is observable (everything up to
  the failed migration is recorded) and the operator re-runs after fixing
  the failure.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered -- premise-check close-audit stories at manifest time**:
  When a sprint story intends to close a set of enumerated TD files, verify
  those files exist BEFORE execution. `ls offices/pm/tech_debt/TD-NNN*.md`
  is a 1-second check that distinguishes "audit + close formally-filed debt"
  (real scope) from "audit confirms never-filed informal references"
  (zero-code scope). Both are valid outcomes but drive very different execution.
- **Gotcha -- auto-memory references are not contracts**: auto-memory surfaces
  items worth checking, not items that must exist. When sprint scope is
  predicated on auto-memory entries (like "some rolled into US-192 but formal
  close not verified"), verify the premise before committing execution
  energy. Sprint-lint could gain a "scope.filesToRead existence check" for
  close-audit story types to catch this at grooming time.
- **Pattern discovered -- outcome-based completion for null-op audits**:
  Per CIO outcome-based-testing rule ("does it work end-to-end?"), when an
  audit trivially completes (nothing to close), the correct move is to
  document findings authoritatively (architecture spec + session-learnings +
  inbox note) and pass the story. Filing retroactive TDs just to close them
  is cargo-cult formalism that violates the CIO drift-observation rule
  (post-hoc TDs add noise without signal).
- **Scope discipline under premise drift**: `scope.filesToTouch` listed 4
  non-existent files + 2 that exist (architecture.md + session-learnings.md).
  Per Scope Fence rule, non-existent entries are no-ops (cannot touch what
  does not exist). Touched only the 2 real entries + the required inbox
  note + standard close-out files (sprint.json, ralph_agents.json,
  progress.txt). `scope.doNotTouch` (deploy/eclipse-obd.service,
  src/pi/display/, requirements-pi.txt) preserved.

## 2026-04-21 - Session 88 - US-219 - Rex (Agent 1)
Task: US-175 Spool data-quality review ritual -- wire report.py + prompts + checklist into runnable script

### What was implemented
- New bash orchestrator `scripts/post_drive_review.sh` wiring four steps:
  Step 1: `python scripts/report.py --drive-id N`    (numeric drive report)
  Step 2: `python scripts/spool_prompt_invoke.py --drive-id N [--dry-run]`
  Step 3: `cat offices/tuner/drive-review-checklist.md`
  Step 4: prints `offices/tuner/reviews/drive-<N>-review.md` + inbox-note
           pointers.
- New Python CLI `scripts/spool_prompt_invoke.py` that REUSES the already-
  shipped server-side prompt pipeline:
  - Imports `_loadSystemMessage`, `_renderUserMessage`,
    `_buildAnalyticsContext`, `_parseRecommendations` from
    `src/server/services/analysis.py`.  No new prompt content, no new
    analysis.  CLI + auto-analyze paths emit byte-identical prompts.
  - Reads Ollama endpoint + model + timeout EXCLUSIVELY from
    `config.json` -> `server.ai.{ollamaBaseUrl, model, apiTimeoutSeconds}`
    with a minimal `${VAR:default}` expander that matches
    `src/common/config/secrets_loader.py` semantics.  Zero hardcoded
    endpoints per US-219 invariant.
  - Graceful-exit contract: empty DB / missing tables / drive not found /
    empty drive window / `OllamaUnreachableError` / `OllamaHttpError` /
    `AiAnalyzerGenerationError` / `KeyError` or `FileNotFoundError` on
    config -- all exit 0 with a human message.  Exit 2 is reserved for
    argparse errors only.  This preserves the invariant that Steps 3+4
    always emit during a live CIO-driven review even when Ollama is
    offline.
- `scripts/report.py`: added `--drive-id` as an argparse alias of
  `--drive` (`dest="drive"`).  No other changes to report.py per
  doNotTouch -- analysis logic untouched.

### Tests added

  `${VAR:default}` expansion, `loadOllamaConfig` env override, drive
  resolution (`latest` + integer + missing + non-integer), dry-run,
  scripted-response live call, empty JSON array, graceful paths for
  empty DB / missing tables / Ollama unreachable / HTTP 5xx / missing
  `server.ai` config block, and argparse surface.
- `tests/scripts/test_post_drive_review_sh.py` -- 11 subprocess tests
  invoking the bash driver via `subprocess.run([bash, ...])`; asserts
  `--help` / `-h`, unknown-flag exit 2, `--drive-id` without value exit
  2, `--drive-id=N` equals syntax, four headers in order, `--dry-run`

  opens a valid schema; forces `sys.executable` via
  `POST_DRIVE_REVIEW_PYTHON` env var so the test harness python is
  used inside the shell script.

### Filename deviation flagged (scope-fence drift-observation)
Story filesToTouch listed `tests/scripts/test_post_drive_review.sh`
(a standalone bash assertion file).  I created
`tests/scripts/test_post_drive_review_sh.py` instead -- a Python
pytest-invokable subprocess wrapper mirroring the more-recent
`test_replay_pi_fixture_sh.py` precedent (Session 57, US-191).  Pure
`.sh` tests are not auto-discovered by pytest and would have required
an additional `.py` wrapper anyway (the `tests/deploy/test_deploy_pi.{sh,py}`
pair pattern).  Keeping it to one file matches convention and reduces
fast-suite collection overhead.  Called out in sprint.json
completionNotes for PM visibility.

### Learnings for future iterations
- **Python default-arg lazy lookup pattern**: `def f(path: Path = _CONFIG_PATH)`
  captures the Path at def-time, so
  `monkeypatch.setattr(module, "_CONFIG_PATH", new_path)` in tests has
  NO effect on the function's default.  Fix: read the module attribute
  inside the function body (`if path is None: path = _CONFIG_PATH`).
  Caught in iteration 1 of the test pass.  Worth remembering for any
  scripts/CLI that uses a module-level path constant as a default arg
  and expects tests to re-point it.
- **Windows cp1252 kills subprocess text-mode decode on box-drawing
  glyphs**: `subprocess.run(..., text=True)` defaults to the system
  encoding, which on Windows is cp1252 and cannot decode U+2550 used
  in the wrapper's section headers.  The reader thread raises
  UnicodeDecodeError and `result.stdout` comes back as `None` (with a
  PytestUnhandledThreadExceptionWarning).  Fix:
  `subprocess.run(..., text=True, encoding='utf-8', errors='replace')`.
  Worth applying to any future subprocess test whose driver uses
  non-ASCII output.
- **Reuse private helpers from an adjacent module when wiring, not
  duplicating**: US-219 is a pure "wire it together" story.  Imported
  `_loadSystemMessage / _renderUserMessage / _buildAnalyticsContext /
  _parseRecommendations` from `src.server.services.analysis` rather
  than reimplementing.  Only the leading underscore was ambiguous, but
  duplicating ~60 lines of `_buildAnalyticsContext` would have
  violated the invariant "WIRES existing pieces. Do NOT write new
  analysis logic or new prompts."  Trade-off accepted: the review
  ritual is now coupled to analysis.py's private surface, which is
  the right coupling for this story's goal (byte-identical prompts
  between CLI and auto-analyze paths).
- **argparse mutual-exclusive groups can alias by `dest`**: adding a
  `--drive-id` alias to report.py's `--drive` required only passing
  both option names + `dest="drive"` to the mutex group's
  `add_argument`.  No separate handler, no None-vs-value disambiguation
  logic.  Cheap, idiomatic, zero behavior change to existing callers.
- **Subprocess test fixture pattern for bash drivers**: use a pytest
  fixture that emits a `DATABASE_URL`-populated SQLite file, pass it
  via `env=` to the subprocess, and gate the entire class on
  `_skipWithoutBash`.  Matches the test_replay_pi_fixture_sh.py
  precedent and keeps the test off the network / off the Pi.

  remaining story is externally gated, a Ralph iteration can legitimately
  close with zero code written. The `ralph_agents.json` note + a short

  also wrong -- CIO already knows; no new judgment needed. ALL_BLOCKED
  (exit 0) is the best fit among the documented tags even though its
  one-line description mentions "claimed by another agent" -- the
  practical meaning is "no work available to this agent for structural
  reasons," which matches.

## 2026-04-23 - US-225
Task: TD-034 close -- US-216 deeper stage behavior wiring (forceKeyOff + no_new_drives flag + sync force-push + pausePolling)

### What was implemented:
- Created src/pi/obdii/pi_state.py -- new singleton table + SCHEMA_PI_STATE + ensurePiStateTable + getNoNewDrives/setNoNewDrives/clearNoNewDrives accessors. CHECK(id=1), INSERT OR IGNORE seed row so reboot preserves operator-set flag. Registered migration in ObdDatabase.initialize as "Created pi_state table (US-225)".
- DriveDetector.forceKeyOff(reason: str) -> bool: acquires self._lock, calls _endDrive(reason), bypasses debounce, safe no-op when STOPPED or STARTING-with-no-session. Returns True only when an active drive was actually terminated.
- _endDrive(reason=None) + _logDriveEvent(..., reason=None) threading: reason goes into connection_log.error_message; NULL preserved for normal debounce drive-end (regression-guarded by test_normalDriveEnd_writesNullErrorMessage).
- _openDriveId gate: getNoNewDrives() check returns None BEFORE nextDriveId(), so drive_counter is NOT incremented when gated.
- SyncClient.forcePush() -> PushSummary: wraps pushAllDeltas with explicit logging + aggregated counts. No invariants bypassed. PushSummary is a slots dataclass.
- ApplicationOrchestrator.pausePolling(reason)/resumePolling(reason): delegates to RealtimeDataLogger.stop/start; separate _pollingPausedForPowerDown flag so BT reconnect path's _dataLoggerPausedForReconnect does not collide. Resume no-op when not paused-for-power-down (does NOT steal BT reconnect resume). start-raises keeps flag True.
- lifecycle.py _wirePowerDownOrchestratorCallbacks rewrite: WARNING = setNoNewDrives(True) + forceSyncPush; IMMINENT = pausePolling(power_imminent) + forceKeyOff(power_imminent); AC-restore = setNoNewDrives(False) + resumePolling(power_restored). Helper methods _setNoNewDrives + _forceSyncPush (lazy SyncClient construction; benign no-op when companion disabled).
- TD-034 annotated CLOSED with disposition table + file list.
- specs/architecture.md Section 10.6 stage-behavior-wiring block (spec said Section 11 but Section 11 is Deployment; 10.6 is US-216 power orchestrator).
- docs/testing.md drill addendum: 4 shell-command observations operators can run post-drain to verify each stage behavior fired.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern: scope-path drift from grooming.** US-225 scope listed src/pi/data/database_schema.py + src/pi/data/database.py but actual code lives at src/pi/obdii/. Spec also said Section 11 of architecture.md but power orchestrator is in Section 10.6. Honored actual paths + noted drift in completionNotes; did NOT widen scope into unrelated sections.
- **Pattern: DriveDetector has its own internal state machine, NOT an EngineStateMachine instance.** The spec groundingRefs line "delegates to existing EngineStateMachine.forceKeyOff" is misleading -- DriveDetector.forceKeyOff must reimplement the end-drive logic directly (call _endDrive with reason), NOT wrap EngineStateMachine. The _lastEngineState attribute on DriveDetector is a US-206 metadata tracker for the drive-summary cold-start ambient rule, not a live state machine.
- **Pattern: reason code goes in connection_log.error_message, not a new column.** Adding a column would require a schema migration + a sync schema bump + a server-side handler change. Using the existing TEXT nullable error_message column keeps the drive_end event_type semantic for analytics (same event_type) while carrying the reason for operators. Regression guard: normal debounce drive-end MUST still emit NULL (pinned by test_normalDriveEnd_writesNullErrorMessage).
- **Pattern: forcePush is a renamed pushAllDeltas + aggregate summary.** No normal-sync invariants bypassed -- the "force" is about explicit intent + single-object return, not about skipping safety gates. The PushSummary dataclass is slot-based for memory + produced from a single iteration of pushAllDeltas results.
- **Pattern: pausePolling/resumePolling use a SEPARATE flag from the BT-reconnect path.** Reusing _dataLoggerPausedForReconnect would cause AC-restore to fight BT reconnect for the resume call when a drain and a BT drop overlap. The two flags are orthogonal; each path tracks its own paused-by-me state and only its own path resumes.
- **Pattern: BT-close on IMMINENT deliberately NOT wired.** The TRIGGER -> systemctl poweroff cascade closes BT via BtResilienceMixin + systemd service-stop; US-211's reconnect classifier owns reattach; US-216 invariant "TRIGGER -> poweroff path stays unchanged" takes priority. Revisit only if a real-drain drill observes BT handle leakage beyond process exit.
- **Pattern: callback failures must not block stage escalation.** PowerDownOrchestrator._invokeCallback already provides broad-exception isolation -- new lifecycle wiring keeps every stage behavior inside a try/except that logs + continues. Regression-guarded by test_warningCallbackRaisesButImminentStillFires + test_imminentCallbackRaisesButTriggerStillFires.

## 2026-04-23 - US-226
Task: Restore Pi->server sync -- last success 2026-04-19; Drive 3 stranded on Pi

### What was implemented:
- NEW pi.sync config section (enabled / intervalSeconds / triggerOn) separate from pi.companionService (which stays the transport config).
- Validator DEFAULTS + new _validatePiSync method (rejects non-list triggerOn, unknown members, disabled-interval-while-enabled).
- _initializeSyncClient in lifecycle.py: constructs SyncClient when pi.sync.enabled; swallows missing-API-key + construction errors as warnings (boot must not crash).
- _shutdownSyncClient for lifecycle symmetry (reference clear; no open connections).
- ApplicationOrchestrator._syncClient + _lastSyncAttemptTime + _syncIntervalSeconds + _syncTriggerOn attributes + syncClient property.
- _maybeTriggerIntervalSync: cheap cadence gate called once per runLoop pass; first call is flush-on-boot; exception-isolated.
- triggerDriveEndSync: hooked into event_router._handleDriveEnd; resets interval cadence so a recently-ended drive does not double-push on next tick.
- 3 new test files / 27 new tests: test_client_config_paths.py (6), test_sync_wiring.py (17), test_pi_to_server_sync_recovery.py (4).
- specs/architecture.md US-226 subsection: pi.sync semantics + recovery playbook.
- docs/testing.md Pi->Server Sync Recovery section: SSH commands for last-sync query + manual trigger + auto-trigger verification.
- Annotated root cause in completionNotes: orchestrator never had an automatic sync trigger; US-154 shipped only the manual sync_now.py CLI with a comment "auto-scheduling is Run-phase scope" that was never implemented.

### Files changed:
- Modified: config.json (new pi.sync section)
- Modified: src/common/config/validator.py (3 DEFAULTS + _validatePiSync + top-level call + mod-history)
- Modified: src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/lifecycle.py (_initializeSyncClient + _shutdownSyncClient + init/shutdown ordering + _syncClient type hint + 2 mod-history entries)
- Modified: src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/core.py (_syncClient + _lastSyncAttemptTime + _syncIntervalSeconds + _syncTriggerOn + syncClient property + _maybeTriggerIntervalSync + triggerDriveEndSync + runLoop wiring + mod-history)
- Modified: src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/event_router.py (triggerDriveEndSync hook in _handleDriveEnd)
- Modified: specs/architecture.md (US-226 subsection under sync_log)
- Modified: docs/testing.md (Pi->Server Sync Recovery section)
- Created: tests/pi/sync/test_client_config_paths.py (6 tests)
- Created: tests/pi/orchestrator/test_sync_wiring.py (17 tests)
- Created: tests/integration/test_pi_to_server_sync_recovery.py (4 tests)

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern: separate 'trigger policy' from 'transport config' in config.json.** pi.companionService governs HOW sync reaches the server (baseUrl, apiKey, retries); pi.sync governs WHEN it fires (enabled, intervalSeconds, triggerOn). Separating the two lets operators disable the trigger without touching the wire protocol and vice versa. When adding a new orchestrator-level scheduler, prefer a new section over overloading an existing transport config.
- **Pattern: boot-time flush is a feature, not a bug.** Initializing _lastSyncAttemptTime to None means the first runLoop pass fires an immediate push. For a Pi that has accumulated rows during an offline period (e.g., Drive 3 stranded since 2026-04-19), this behavior automatically drains the backlog on next boot. Interval cadence kicks in after that first push.
- **Pattern: interval trigger MANDATORY when sync enabled.** The validator enforces that 'interval' is in triggerOn when pi.sync.enabled=true. This is defensive design given the US-229 drive_end detection bug -- if the only trigger is drive_end and drive_end is broken, rows strand. Catching this at config-load time is better than at observed-data-loss time.
- **Pattern: exception-safe sync triggers.** Both _maybeTriggerIntervalSync and triggerDriveEndSync wrap pushAllDeltas() in broad-exception capture. A transport hiccup, a DB lock contention, or a malformed response never crashes runLoop. The per-table FAILED status already preserves the high-water mark so the next tick resends.
- **Pattern: flush-on-boot race with simulate=True.** ApplicationOrchestrator construction is side-effect-free even with simulate=True -- _initializeSyncClient is safe to call directly in tests without going through the full _initializeAllComponents chain. This isolates the sync plumbing tests from the rest of the init sequence.
- **Gotcha: the story's language about 'add or rename pi.sync section' can mislead.** The actual production config has pi.companionService (for transport) but no pi.sync (for trigger). Treating pi.sync as a NEW section preserves US-149/US-151/US-225 behavior and avoids cascading changes into SyncClient + scripts/sync_now.py + test_sync_client.py. Read scope carefully before renaming cross-cutting config keys.

## 2026-04-23 - US-228
Task: Fix US-206 drive_summary NULL on cold-start -- timing bug drive_start before first IAT reading

### What was implemented:
- New `SummaryRecorder.backfillFromSnapshot(driveId, snapshot, fromState) -> SummaryBackfillResult` with COALESCE semantics: UPDATEs NULL sensor columns with candidate values, never overwrites a non-NULL stored value. Warm-restart ambient rule auto-preserved because `buildSummaryFromSnapshot` already zeroes ambient for non-cold-start `fromState`.
- New `SummaryBackfillResult(driveId, filled: frozenset[str], complete: bool)` frozen dataclass. `filled` is a subset of the three column aliases (ambient/battery/baro) describing what this call wrote. `complete` is the early-exit signal for the detector tick loop -- True when all applicable columns are non-NULL (cold start: all three; warm restart: battery + baro, ambient is N/A).
- New `DEFAULT_DRIVE_SUMMARY_BACKFILL_SECONDS = 60` constant in `drive/types.py` + matching `DetectorConfig.driveSummaryBackfillSeconds` field + `_loadConfig` now pulls `pi.analysis.driveSummaryBackfillSeconds` with the default.
- New DriveDetector state: `_driveSummaryBackfillDriveId / _driveSummaryBackfillDeadline / _driveSummaryBackfillComplete / _driveSummaryBackfillFromState`. `_armDriveSummaryBackfill(startTime)` called from `_startDrive` right after `_captureDriveStartSummary`. Window cleared at `_endDrive`.
- New `_maybeBackfillDriveSummary(now)` called from `processValue` each tick. Cheap early-exit (complete / past-deadline / not-RUNNING / no recorder / no snapshot source / empty snapshot). Otherwise dispatches `backfillFromSnapshot`; flips complete=True when result.complete.
- `config.json` gets `pi.analysis.driveSummaryBackfillSeconds: 60` for explicit discoverability alongside the other drive-detection keys.
- `specs/architecture.md` Section 5 drive_summary subsection gains a "Cold-start backfill (US-228)" paragraph + new invariants list covering COALESCE semantics, warm-restart ambient suppression, and backfill-disarms-at-drive-end.
- `docs/testing.md` gains a CIO-facing "drive_summary Cold-Start Validation (US-228)" section with SSH commands, expected cold-start vs warm-restart outcomes, and the operator fallback path (bump backfill window, grep journalctl).

### Files changed:
- Modified: `src/pi/obdii/drive_summary.py` (added SummaryBackfillResult + backfillFromSnapshot method; +~110 lines)
- Modified: `src/pi/obdii/drive/detector.py` (backfill state + arm/tick methods; +~90 lines)
- Modified: `src/pi/obdii/drive/types.py` (DEFAULT_DRIVE_SUMMARY_BACKFILL_SECONDS + DetectorConfig field + toDict entry)
- Modified: `config.json` (pi.analysis.driveSummaryBackfillSeconds=60)
- Modified: `specs/architecture.md` (Cold-start backfill subsection under drive_summary section)
- Modified: `docs/testing.md` (Cold-Start Validation section + mod-history)
- Created: `tests/pi/obdii/test_drive_summary_cold_start.py` (8 unit tests: bug repro + fill all three + fill only available + no-op on full row + warm-restart-skip-ambient + 3 edge cases)
- Created: `tests/pi/integration/test_drive_summary_backfill.py` (5 integration tests: empty-at-start-backfilled-across-ticks + complete-flag-early-exit + window-timeout + warm-restart-ambient-rule + drive-end-disarms-backfill)

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **COALESCE-semantics UPDATE pattern for backfill writers.** When a writer has to INSERT early with partial data and later UPDATE missing columns, the "don't overwrite non-NULL with NULL" invariant is critical. Straight UPSERT replaces column-by-column, which clobbers earlier good values if a later snapshot has NULLs. Solution: SELECT first, decide which columns are currently NULL AND have non-NULL candidates, then UPDATE those columns only. Keeps the writer path linear (one SELECT + one UPDATE at most) without resorting to SQL `COALESCE(...)` expressions (simpler to reason about in Python + easier to test).
- **Backfill-window state belongs on the caller, not the writer.** Initially considered making SummaryRecorder track the per-drive backfill deadline internally, but the writer is stateless (one connection-open per call, no per-drive context). Putting the deadline/complete-flag on DriveDetector as the tick coordinator keeps the recorder pure + gives the detector one O(1) early-exit at the top of the tick loop.
- **Pre-flight reproduction pays off twice.** The story asked me to synthesize drive_start with an empty snapshot to confirm the bug (acceptance #1). Doing that revealed a SECOND latent bug: the existing captureDriveStart UPSERT can clobber non-NULL cols with NULL when a later partial snapshot arrives. The COALESCE-semantics backfill path prevents that too -- belt + suspenders. Would not have noticed without the three-call pre-flight script.
- **"Complete" semantics for warm restart is a footgun without the N/A escape hatch.** The first implementation of `backfillFromSnapshot` said `complete = all three cols non-NULL`, which would mean a warm-restart drive could NEVER reach complete=True (ambient is permanent NULL by invariant). That would leave the detector polling forever until window expiry. Fix: `ambientComplete = stored_ambient is not None OR NOT cold_start` -- warm-restart drives satisfy ambient trivially, so the detector short-circuits as soon as battery + baro arrive.
- **Scope bleed on DetectorConfig.** Adding a new detector-config field requires editing `drive/types.py` (where DetectorConfig lives). Story's filesToTouch didn't list types.py but did list detector.py + require the window to be config-driven. Inline hardcoding would have violated CLAUDE.md's "no hardcoded values" rule, so types.py was the structurally-required touch site. Flagged in completionNotes for PM visibility.
- **Drive 3's actual drive_summary row is unfixable.** The backfill only runs during the bounded window after drive_start. Drive 3's row was written 2026-04-23 early afternoon; nothing triggers backfill anymore. US-227 truncate will NOT touch drive_id=3. Row stays all-NULL. Flagged in story stopCondition #3 -- did not take the retroactive backfill path.
- **Pattern: ambient "applicable" flag driven by cold-start rule.** Reusing `AMBIENT_COLD_START_STATES` / `_isColdStart` for the "is ambient applicable?" decision makes the completion check match the write-path rule exactly. No need for a second definition of "warm restart" in the backfill logic.
---

## 2026-04-23 - [US-232] (Session 102, Rex)
Task: TD-035 close -- retry loop responds to SIGTERM within 2s

### What was implemented:
- Added optional `shutdownEvent: threading.Event | None` to `ObdConnection.__init__`. Retry loop checks `shutdownEvent.is_set()` before each attempt and uses `shutdownEvent.wait(timeout=delay)` instead of `time.sleep(delay)` when an event is plumbed in. When the event wakes the loop, return False cleanly with state DISCONNECTED.
- Added `shutdownEvent` parameter to `ReconnectLoop.__init__` and `buildDefaultReconnectLoop`. When provided, the default `sleepFn` becomes `event.wait(timeout=backoff)`, and `_shouldExit` also consults `shutdownEvent.is_set()` so an event set during the sleep aborts the loop on the next iteration.
- Orchestrator `ApplicationOrchestrator.__init__` now creates `self._shutdownEvent: threading.Event`, exposed via a `shutdownEvent` property.
- `SignalHandlerMixin._handleShutdownSignal` now also `self._shutdownEvent.set()` on both first (graceful) and second (force) signals, so any retry loop blocked in a backoff sleep wakes within ms of SIGTERM.
- `LifecycleMixin._initializeConnection` passes `shutdownEvent=self._shutdownEvent` to `createConnectionFromConfig`, which forwards it into `ObdConnection`.
- `BtResilienceMixin._defaultLoopFactory` passes `shutdownEvent=self._shutdownEvent` into `buildDefaultReconnectLoop`.
- Backwards compat: when no event is passed (legacy callers, unit-level tests), the retry paths fall back to `time.sleep` exactly as before. Two dedicated tests guard this non-regression (`test_connectRetryLoop_noShutdownEvent_preservesTimeSleep` + `test_reconnectLoop_noShutdownEvent_preservesExistingBehavior`).
- TD-035 file annotated Closed with reference to US-232.

### Files changed:
- Modified: `src/pi/obdii/obd_connection.py` (shutdownEvent kwarg + event.wait in retry)
- Modified: `src/pi/obdii/reconnect_loop.py` (shutdownEvent kwarg + _eventAwareSleep + _shouldExit consults event)
- Modified: `src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/core.py` (self._shutdownEvent + shutdownEvent property)
- Modified: `src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/signal_handler.py` (handler sets event)
- Modified: `src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/lifecycle.py` (plumb event into createConnectionFromConfig)
- Modified: `src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/bt_resilience.py` (plumb event into buildDefaultReconnectLoop)
- Created: `tests/pi/obdii/test_sigterm_responsiveness.py` (4 tests -- ObdConnection retry loop)
- Created: `tests/pi/obdii/test_reconnect_loop_sigterm.py` (6 tests -- ReconnectLoop backoff)
- Modified: `offices/pm/tech_debt/TD-035-collector-bt-retry-ignores-sigterm.md` (Closed annotation)

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **threading.Event is the stdlib idiom for interruptible sleep** when a signal handler and a worker (or the same main thread in a blocking loop) need to coordinate a wake. `event.wait(timeout=N)` returns True when set, False on natural expiry -- the distinction is exactly what you want for "did SIGTERM fire during the sleep?" logic. The test harness drives this from a helper thread that calls `event.set()` after 100ms; no OS signal module involvement, so the test is portable to Windows CI.
- **Scope-fence note: don't blindly follow filesToTouch.** The story listed `src/pi/main.py` for the signal handler, but the orchestrator's `SignalHandlerMixin` already owns SIGTERM/SIGINT with a load-bearing double-signal force-exit pattern. Adding a separate main() handler would fight for signal ownership (last registered wins via `signal.signal()`). Correct scope was to extend `_handleShutdownSignal` inside the mixin to also set the shared event. Flagged in feedback.scopeFenceNote so Marcus can see the substitution.
- **Test against a 60s-cap backoff even when the target is 2s.** Using a short `retryDelays=[1,2]` wouldn't prove the event wakes the sleep (the sleep would end naturally in 3s either way). Sizing the test to a schedule that would classically take >60s -- and asserting <3s elapsed -- is what actually exercises the wake. The same principle applied to the pre-set test (the pre-set path must skip ALL sleeps, which requires a long-tail schedule to be detectable).
- **Compose shutdownEvent with the existing shouldExitFn seam rather than replacing it.** ReconnectLoop already had `shouldExitFn` (from US-211). US-232 adds `shutdownEvent` as a peer, not a replacement. `_shouldExit` now returns True if EITHER is set, and `_sleepFn` defaults to event-aware when an event is provided. This preserves US-211's custom-predicate callers while giving the orchestrator a simpler wiring path.
- **Backwards-compat is a first-class test case for an opt-in seam.** The two "no event passed -> unchanged behavior" tests (one per class) are what let Ralph touch the connection + reconnect hot paths without fear of an existing caller breaking. Worth making this the second test you write after the happy-path test.
